The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by means of a medicinal solution modifying the head, either two or three times, according to what is useful and agreeable to the patient's habit; and then make the patient drink the head of the patient again.

Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called “closed” because its head is made in the shape of a nail or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small appearance; put out the painful limb, and hold your hand steady and lightly touch the fire until half of the thickness of the hair is burned; and hold your hand away from the artery, which should not be burned, and there should be plenty of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, take it out; then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and cure the limb until it is healed. de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, take it out; then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and cure the limb until it is healed. And if you are going to cauterize this embolism with the cautery called "cultellare," at the very tip, keep the artery in this embolism that is not ancient.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cauterize an embolism as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cautery must precede medical treatment and that it does not suffice, then you must avoid the cautery called "cultellare" as long as it is blunt; and sign out the limb by drawing a line a half inch long, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and do not move anything until the bone; and be careful of the jaw that it does not move when you move, and that it does not cause you pain, and be careful of the displacement of blood from the artery when it is cauterized, or when it has been cauterized for a long time; and that you do not do anything rash or beyond your knowledge, and that you are not a student or an experienced physician; and leave the work in progress; but I will tell you how to retain blood when the artery is cauterized, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans. Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those which move with phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery which appears to come from drying and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture which is made of fumes of hydras and vomiting of head and gargling, and this is not worth it, then you must cauterize the patient with two cauters: one at the root of the ear, and the other at the temple, and the third at the junction of the two upper eyelids; and put the cautery on the part which is open safely, and make the cautery in the place of the head of the ear below a little below the corner of the eye, and another in the temple as long as a bean; and leave the cautery on for as long as half of the current is burned. This is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez. de litargie	De litargie.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	From litargie.

If he is sane, it is good; and if not, do two cauteries on the head, descending juice until it reaches the collar, and leave an inch of space between each cautery; and cure as with the others. de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head.

de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy

de l’awe des eulz	Or if you see a burn cauterized in making multiple pricks throughout the burn. This method of cautery soothes the brain immediately; then put on a moist bandage of wool and grease with gelline.</start_of_turn>

de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is like this

Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hair grow long and even, then make a parchment of the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live chalk, each a third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly, if it does not cool down, and put on the shape that you have made like a myrtle leaf, and put on the master’s eggs; and if the patient suffers only from oil, if you must operate in oil, and if there are two of them, put on the cotton wool soaked in oil; and the patient’s head should be in its natural position and put your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once or twice every time the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for he feels the bite as well as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have performed this for a long time, if the bones are stiff with medicine, you must have it.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size, and according to that be their constraints; and do not respond to him the right way to him who is the student of this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	And know that when you cure fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your cure does you no good, then you must burn it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in order; and hold his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, do not lower his head; afterwards put a piece of cotton soaked in oil of vitriol or in vinegar on the wound; then burn the cautery which is part: and touch it to the wound as if it were a feather of goosefoot, gather it up so that it is worth the work.  If you see that the wound is pointed from one side to the other, or if you see that it is as if a thread were torn; but in any case, that which is touched is more worth than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells out, and in its course it becomes soft and dry; when it is closed, if the swelling, and in its course it drives out the hair; after that, put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part where there is no feeling in the neighbourhood of the oil, so that your hand does not tremble; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and compress it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you begin the cautery treatment right up to the bone, that would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If this does not happen, if you begin the cautery once more, and this time you succeed, and leave it for three days; after that put on moist cotton wool around the wound and let the drying dressing cure until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is still not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and leave it as it comes in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cautery for fistula of which no ancient author has spoken
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a fistula, and open the cavity; after that put into the opening one camel’s eye of gut which is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it in the amount of a third of a palm; and hold your hand or forearm firmly, and the patient does not move a finger, until the melted wax drains down to its oil; and it is fitting to put on the oil to the patient a soft cotton swab in the palm of the hand or on the forearm. The wax if it is too hard makes a fistula, and the same for mere curiosity without any benefit.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if that does not suffice, if you must administer a pierce to the bone, and bring the fistula back to the bone as it should be in its proper place.

de l’aposteme de la goule	to the apex of the shoulder
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the swelling comes up to the root of the gullet or the eye, or the palate, or the root of the teeth, after that it must be perforated and drained and becomes filled and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not be of any benefit: therefore it must be that you cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or back; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would do in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the swelling comes up to the root of the gullet or the eye, or the palate, or the root of the teeth, after that it must be perforated and drained and becomes filled and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not be of any benefit: therefore it must be that you cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or back; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would do in its chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you must cure it with medicine and that will be of no use, therefore put the patient’s head in your hand; after that wash the cautery which will form later on in part as if you were putting on a pin; and put some cautery inside the tooth immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that let go of your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and rinse vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part for this reason, when it is confirmed that the limb was moving, the soft tissue softens and contracts, and the moisture becomes dry.
de la dolor des dens	And in part for this reason, when it is confirmed that the limb was moving, the soft tissue softens and contracts, and the moisture becomes dry.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures are of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the burn and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If the burn is such that you take a burr of beech, and put the end in a spoon of iron or steel; then take cotton and wrap over the point of a needle, and moisten with oil, and put over the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cool; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth.  And if you see that there is too much moisture and cotton on the burr, take off the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery is applied with fire if it is like a burnt cane of iron or flax, and let it be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient’s mouth; after that, burn the cautery, so that it forms like this afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, for the pain will be great as much on one side as on the other
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you must make the patient swallow well with good soft food in the heat of this cautery, and then draw out the tongue forcefully; that is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Do as you please with the cautery, and according to what you are able; and this is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	And the size of the wound on the penis and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are some of these wounds or chieftains and there is no moisture, or if these are old wounds which I have cauterized or chieftains from an old woman; and find the wound just like a stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if no blood appears, we must make just as good a wound as if it were a stone. In other wounds coming or chieftains, because these which come from the groin and from the roots of the ears, the opening must be made if it is at all possible every day, in order to prevent the swelling; and the treatment must be made as it is fitting.

Then cure the wound of abscesses and sutures until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The formation of the cancer.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by soluble medicines; after that, perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go down further than the throat, and do not prick more than is necessary.

de la toust	When moisture prevails over the veins due to a cold complexion, then it is recommended that the patient be first treated with soothing medicines; after that, perform the cautery at the root of the jaw, and keep it from reaching the throat, and do not be afraid of causing pain only in this place. de la mice	The mouse is small and harmless,

Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in part that you take two green and fresh barley grains, and grind them with a little fat, and put them on the groin, thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind them; and leave them for three hours, forasmuch that the patient does not feel the burning sensation anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter or bathe until the flesh is slightly swollen, and then make him enter or lie down, and the pain will go away and be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And wounds that no one must use fire cautery of such medicines, except after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And thus Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with pieces of sponge, if it helps moisture; and must be done cautiously.</start_of_turn>
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in oil abundantly, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the great toe and the one that is called the fossicle.</start_of_turn
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dry pieces of sponge, burn them over fire until they are charred, and put them on the lint, and leave them until they are stained; and do this several times, and do not stop doing it until you think that enough has been done until the swelling has gone down and the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "sponge cautery".</start_of_turn
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things of cold expanding matter, none of these symptoms is worth resorting to cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is devoid of foul pills or other things of the like, that one should make three lines signed with a needle on the back, in the loin or in the place where the pain persists; and make three or four cauteries as much as the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called the "needle"; and if you see that it is necessary, make two or three cauteries at the middle of the cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that it has burst open the underlying flesh as soon as it appears, and fear; and you find it in the lower spine of the back and on us appears what comes after the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize with the fire according to this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns a part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the burn penetrates to the spine too much, cauterize around the spine two or three lines from the point where the burn penetrates. Keep the points close to each other.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the burn is done, keep the limb sound as we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery too close to the nerves.</start_of_turn
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that swells every limb, and when pain originates from the bone itself, that is when the sufferer cries out "podagre" in pain; and when the cause is cold and the disease does not yield to medicine, if it is cured by cautery in part: make a mouth of cautery around the joint of the limb, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the bone, if you make the burn with all the cautery, say "point".</start_of_turn
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the joints and other parts, and this happens often, make the burn on each joint three times with the olive cautery; and if you must do more, make more, but do not hold your hand too long in case the burn gets burned.</start_of_turn
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pain descends down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pain is as far as the hands, if you prick twice at the base of the nail; and if there remains no pain after that, prick once on each joint and on the root of the hand; and if the pain comes down to the buttocks or the shoulder blades, burn a part of it, and give good governance to the patient and prescribe medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the disease
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones descend as coions, it is new; if you see it cured, do not trust that it is healed; and if it uses things that release its belly, so that the pain descends from its belly; then make it sit on its buttocks between your hands, and command that it hold its flank until the bones are repaired, and keep it still at your thighs, and mark with a sign on the edge of the fracture above the collarbone, and do all that is like half a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery like this:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is limp and has a dull sensation.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then bind the limb to its place; and he holds your hand so that it does not slip back; and work well the wound on the patient, and put a cushion under his elbow and under his thumb, and another under his wrist; then put the cautery on the sign at the whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you burn the bone, and if you do not reach the bone the first time, try again another time as long as you live until you reach the bone; and be wary that the limb does not swell when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this means the patient does not die, or any other evil
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And soaks that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be known that the cautery of small wounds must be subtle in measure, and of great people also great in measure; after three days cure the body of the burn until the scab is bony; after that cure other ailments until they are healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and it must be known that their movements must be restful, so that the swelling does not arise when he walks to his bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be carried in a good litter, and carry him for forty days more; and let him rest well, that he work little and take care of himself not to eat too much or drink too much, and not to eat too coarsely; and when he has learned this he will be entirely healed
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall tell you afterwards about the treatment of the heel in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the root of the belly</start_of_turn>
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come from other parts and are known, and you see that they do not grow further, if you do not prick them with the cautery at their root, hold the eyes steadily as they do not move until they grow.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the wound and make a line along the width of the wound, and another beyond, and hold your hand firmly with all your might.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more fluid.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in no limb</start_of_turn
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether of bone or flesh, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical treatment is not sufficient, then it is recommended to cauterize with the cautery called “pointed,” and to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its width and thinness, its toughness and its capacity for twisting and its pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery upon that one, for it is customary that it must move to the adjacent limb, so that you may make the cauteries while the patient is sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, or from sitting or from any other cause, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is advised that it be cauterized with the cautery known as "poins," or with such cautery as is appropriate for the length of the limb, its width and weakness, its flexibility and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat it. Indeed, it is customary that it must move towards the limb that is nearest, because it is believed that thus one can make the cauteries as long as the patient remains healthy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases are never aided by cautery in any way, and even the disease which comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cautery? Take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not delay, for you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole disease; then make five cauteries on the head: one at the new root, and the other towards the front at the end of the beard; and two on the two corners, and one behind on the shoulder; and leave as much hand as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as much as the scabs fall out so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before you
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is a general looseness of the humors throughout; and it becomes manifest, as it is fitting that you should cauterize with these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, that is to say, cauterize on the low side of the neck, and two on the spine of the shoulder, three on the spine of the back, and one great one on the armpit and one other below, two on the two scapulae, two on the flanks, two on the tendons of the wrist and hand, and one on every joint of the fingers and toes, and on the fossae of the hands; and be wary of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the heel or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And so it is that the more the physician makes use of the cautery, the more he renders aid, and the more he profits; and so it is that the patients feel no pain from the cautery as much as if they were feeling no pain at all, for the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery must be great and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you find in the handling of things.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment with flour poultices several times with honey and other remedies until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and dressings, and it is not well, then one must cauterize the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery penetrate deeply as much as the nerve; and then cure with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never must the cautery be performed with the hand and the arm and the back, at the issue of a nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is bony it swells; and in any case nothing must intervene between them unless one is familiar with the limb and the issues of the moving nerves and bones.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils and plasters, and is not completely healed, then one should make cautery on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery be performed at a distance from the bone. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be done on the hand, foot or back, at the exit of a nerve that makes the limb numb. And if it is a bone that causes the swelling, nothing should interfere except for those who are skilled in bones and the issues of nerves that move the limb.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine has no power over it, then one should make cautery with a needle at a distance, according to the thickness of the swelling, until the blood is seen to bleed, and let it bleed; then cure with flour of wheat from time to time, with lentils and rose oil, and plantain leaves, and colon and aloe, half of each; mix them all together and bind them with a bandage, and leave it until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes to the beginning, and you see it stop, if you burn it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that one must burn at the middle of the boil; and all these things do not seem good to me, because I fear that it will ulcerate and become corrupted, and I would rather leave it alone never to do it again; and the better thing is to burn around it, with the cautery which is called the "circle", as we have said before.</start_of_turn
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati," and it delays in healing or because of the excess it makes or because of the swelling of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and there is a lot of blood, or for fear; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of the small cauteries by pricking; and afterwards leave it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if thou seest her perish with all the cautery, if thou dost burn the cautery too much: this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have perceived the heat, and be such cauteries that the patient feels a tingling in part as the course of the decay is joyous.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards cure as long as it is perfectly sound
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," and is nothing but the eating away of a limb, for it causes the limbs to swell as if by fire.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb which you can treat with fire cautery, then burn the nails small and great according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after you have cauterized all the parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains of it except the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized parts ointment with oil so that the blisters from the fire become ossified, and all the corruption
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of oily substances which cause swelling.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the hair has not begun to grow back, it is good; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this symptom is never cured by ordinary medicine; but indeed fire cautery is of greater help. As I have already said in the division, take as much as you need of it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The burn cure by iron. Another method of disease that is called "corrodens" and is nothing but the weakening of a limb, for it causes the limbs to swell as much as the flames do to dry linen. If you see this disease in a limb that can suffer from an overall burn, then cover the small and great nails closely together according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; then burn all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains but bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the burned limbs and burn with oil until the burn blisters are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of the wounds that remain. And if after two days the wound has not healed, it is good; and if this is not the case, repeat the burn on what remains of the corrupted limbs. This weakening is never cured by water medicine instead of fire burn; but every burn is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of water medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often there arises a disease called “clos” according to our understanding, and it is a great burden that boils up like blood
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery of fire if it is that you are shaving I cautery cheveit as well as is a pin of wool, and be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the head of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; after that put all around above the head as far as it goes to the front of the head; and leave it for three days until it begins to ooze pus; then make an embolus of wild mallow broth with wool, and leave the embolus on all night, and close the wound tightly and it will be healed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound by stretching the skin until it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by boils many times happen and on hands and in feet, if you must know that you must bring an aqua cautery of hot water; and this is in part: take a sickle of barley or iron, or a pin of wool, and put on the wound and the dressing, that is to say, nails of barley; and put the sickle on so that it pinches all around, then put a little of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the sickle comes to the root of the wound, and can find the hot water going deep just to the root; and give the patient a little dose of the hot water an hour; then leave it like that, and it will break out all at once at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do another after the other, until you have scraped off all that is on the body, then cure the wounds that cause carbuncles.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When the limbs tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other, if you command .iiij. cautery or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between the shoulder blades; and .i. cautery or pinch, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the healing of the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When the limbs tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other, if you command three or four cautery marks on the spine of the back, one cautery mark between the shoulder blades; and one cautery mark or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the healing of the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear by discharges the body bathes, or boils filled with pus, that come from corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it be convenient at the first when they appear that we make cautery upon every head of the abscess: a subtle cautery of mustard seed, so that the point be grasped by the fire, or of aristegall root long, or the lenticular cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never before we cauterize when they appear, according to this manner, that they do not cross forward, but are broken by the fluid from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.</start_of_turn
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there is often a great outflow of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is often a matter of great distress.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming down your thumb, and no blood comes out anymore; then take some olive oil cautery pieces, small and large as you like, until they are all red; then press [it] in, that is to say, large or small as is suitable for the wound and the limb in which the artery is obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as necessary.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out violently when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of another cautery that is already on the fire immediately.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the limb is restored; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and do this with such care that when the artery is large, it can be closed by itself without any other method than those we have mentioned: or by cautery, or by extraction if it is not treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to close the wound. And be certain to bind and strain afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb with tight draping or with the placing of hot things upon it, or other similar things, will gain no benefit from it unless it is of use in this case
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no remedy and no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still until it is healed from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that the wound is not frozen and does not swell and heal; and make inquiries of what is necessary to cauterize and administer medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said or in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or to apply hot medicine, and to inquire about the odium, the cause, the instruments, and the forms of the cautery; and in this chapter we shall speak of the treatment of wounds from the chest to the foot, and I shall deal with this matter in the same way as before, for it is easier for me to speak of these things in order.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must tell you, dear sir, that there is more peril and fear in this chapter than in the previous one concerning cautery, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not act rashly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many times people come to grief through rashness.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have suffered so greatly from their ailments that they move lightly from the fear of their disease, and from the greatness of their malice; and of these things we must have fear.</start_of_turn>
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these things there are those who will tell you: “Wait, I am strong enough”; and the disease is desperate.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not enough for me that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner; but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not foolishly delay but prudently from what you are certain, and from what you have taken and lost; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is either restored or converted; and this will help you to obtain good renown, glory, and memory in the long run.</start_of_turn>
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you are doing well to understand and to grieve, and if you are stirred by the Holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selon ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’à piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have ordered from the chief until the foot, because you will find it lighter than what you have had to bear
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have ordered from the chief until the foot, because you will find it lighter than what you have had to bear.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease leave so quickly as in the countryside; and all those whom I have seen with it grow desperate. For this reason, it seems to me that it is worth omitting the work in parts for the cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have often seen children in whom the head of the shoulder was dislocated by moisture, and the head grew so large that it could not be supported; and there was such great moisture that it became blood, and this moisture if it is collected between the bones above the elbow and the bones below, and the work is done when the moisture is between the elbow and the bones, and the incision is small, that you must make a large incision; and it must be as long as this moisture has lasted.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture swells the bone, and you see the teeth of the jaw protruding outwards in a portion, and there is an acute pain when you press with your hand from within, and this does not subside: if you suspect that the jaw is fractured, make two incisions as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out all the moisture with force.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After that, drain the blood clots and humours, and pour wine and oil, and leave it until the fifth hour; then remove it, and close the wound with sutures and stitches, and leave the head exposed, and give the patient dry meat in place of the moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to look or open the opening of the abscess, and the collection of fluid; for never is it before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.</start_of_turn>
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides murió dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.
de reume	If the vein or the artery is opened, and the liquid is instilled, and you do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; and let blood flow freely, so that the patient does not die from excessive bleeding and discharge of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no other disease which is called "catarrh" which has pus or swelling, and when the disease is old and medicine cannot cure it, then the only cure is to cauterize with that which will cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, that you do not cover the patient’s head; after that, wipe the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open; then pull out the patient’s neck with all your might; then look to see if the vein has burst, and the upper and lower lips are below the ears, and if so, restore them; then mark the places of the sutures, and close one and the other with a needle of two parts, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, which is done by means of the large head of the needle
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, loosen the tweezers from the artery and join at the top, cutting as much as two thumbs together.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is joined, if you do not hold it steadily, it will immediately burst.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on feeling, if you deem it necessary, measure the amount of space of three fingers, then mark and hold until the bone; whatever it is that you must force out blood if it is six cubits, and more or less according to what the patient can suffer, and the refilling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains over the point where the artery was pierced, if the edges of the incision do not meet, then strain the wound and bind it, and cure the bleeding until it stops.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on examination, if you measure the quantity of the space of two fingers' breadth, then mark the point and proceed until you reach the bone; and what you must do is apply pressure if it is more than two finger-breadths, or less. According to what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the wound that you have made does not bleed, then strain the wound and tie it, and leave it to heal.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient secretion comes and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and the chalor in the temples and the old saliva forsened and similar things, it is medicated by means of medical cures and all that does not help, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is as follows: if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating; and when it is opened, strain his neck the patient with some cloths, then wipe the area of no rough hair, and raise the area of warm water until the artery opens clearly; then take the sponge and that is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently pull away the skin until you reach the artery, then hold it high with forceps, and remove the dressing from the area below the wound; and if the artery is delicate, if the nail has caught on the bone, then close that part according to the quantity of two fingers.</start_of_turn>
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not fixed, if I do not jump with all my might.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from .vj. cubits, just up to .iij.; and if the artery is large, it is convenient to ligate it in .ij. loops with a strong thread of silk, so that no blood will be seen before the wound is sutured; and withdraw blood steadily. Then cut away the excess that is between the .ij. loops in that middle hour, and if you see that, if you wish, cauterize with a fine cautery needle until the blood is clotted; and that is the perfect remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful in finishing off moisture: for this reason it is of greater aid than moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the cavity with much cotton and make good stitches; and when one removes them, if one has cured with dry medicines which cause new hair and stitches, as long as it is healthy; and if without support of the artery as much as one does work, if you are in a hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use the cavity of vitriol and strain your hand, as it should be; and if you do not have this present, if you must take out the cavity, you must do so while the vessel is not frozen, and rise the cold water until the vessel stops moving, and strain as it should be; and what is more painful and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting from a third to a fourth of an inch, but the cutting should be well spaced to prevent it from lasting too long.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.

des larmes	And must have between the joints a space of one inch; then when you have signified the nails, let the loop burn until it reaches the bone, and close the vein with two nails; and let them be spaced between the joints, for they are not firmly joined by this cautery in all cases; and this is the form of the cautery.

de la gresle	De la gresle.

de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The oily discharge is enclosed in paper tissues and appears more abundant in women than in men, and causes itching at their eyes, and they come out with morning sickness, and do not dare to look at the sunlight for that the tears hurry away from their eyes; and because they lie with their faces downwards, and sleep on them, and their paper tissues are wet with moisture that swells and appears covered with the oily discharge that comes out in the oil.
