And thus the work is that the patient puts his head in its place; then take one cloth of linen, and make a loop resembling a circle according to the quantity of exinach in the upper part, then put it on; and press on your belly from both sides, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make an incision at the navel, about the size of a wound made to the vein; and do not make it any larger than the wound made to the vein; and stretch the leather as much as you can while you see the exinach. And in many cases comes exinach from the incision, like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tissue from the entire piece of charcoal between your hands at the flanks, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not touch the incision, that you do not go beyond the navel, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the dislocation does not spontaneously reduce at the beginning of the incision, if you widen the incision slightly until it opens; then grasp it as we have said, then moisten the drape in oil and water, and place over it, and strain of bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such people exist who crush it and put it on to corrupt that moisture that remains immobile
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is safe.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the vein bursts suddenly, the cure of plugging the blood clot is to leave it whole as long as it is steady.
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs attached other than their natural state, and are enclosed, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases like tears that are accustomed to flow and soften papers and gum, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the fire cautery, or it is done by incision and suture or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the chief of the patient in your left hand, then draw the paper from the oil at your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a hook at every thread of the paper; either cut the edge of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs, and take out one thread from under the paper, and draw it to the end; then make in the lower part of the paper, the hairs attached, at all the breadth from the great tear to the little one; then take out one thread and put under the paper a little patch of cotton and bandage, and sign on the paper a figure like that of a thrush, and all that is necessary is that the figure be according to the quantity you see that the paper that is destined to you is elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If the vein bursts suddenly, the cure of plugging the blood clot is to leave it whole as long as it is steady.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold this that which is above down with small forces equally in conformity with the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the teeth firmly, and the thing is not even, take a needle or two and pass a thread through the figure; and pass another thread loosely from the great toe, and the second thread loosely from the little toe, and join the two threads evenly; then stretch your hand evenly, and stretch all the skin over that which you have marked, as we have told; then join the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and similar soothing dressings. Never again shall there be anything more converted than the hair of a hare: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the sutures in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for armpit hair is as follows: convert the hair and fat according to what has been said, then make three hairs by art, and three fine threads as long as the hair and as wide as a span; and hold two threads of each hand. Then assemble the one and the other securely over that which covers the oil of the hair, and strain the three hairs from the three parts. Leave for a few days, and the skin which has been strained will wither and darken and will fall out, until it comes out by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and the arrow is extracted, the hair will not grow again; and this is the form of two nails that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and breadth.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is immediately a thread of silk subtle; then assemble the threads and know each one from the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be equal; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not touch the chief of the thread; then place the patient's chief in its place; and let go of the sun if the work is completed, for this is a subtle and minor work, then withdraw the needle at all the chase to the root of the hair to the joint; and make it pierce in the membrane as much as you can until you have pulled it out from its natural position; then draw out the hair until it reaches the chase, and withdraw the needle from the chase if there is one or two or three or more; then draw out your hand until the vein is completely withdrawn from the chase with the natural position of the hand.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from its piercement through sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair has healed in its place and the wound has closed.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the putrefaction comes to the head, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes about by wound, or by bite, or by cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of working in this is that you make that suture, and dry the flesh, and put in there some linen threads, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything except use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but there is need for emollient things, such as fennel; and the rose of water or violet and poppy seeds boiled in any oil, and it wraps around a bandage, and treats it in this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from its former shape; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except in addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	De la char qui vient en l’oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called by the swelling that really exists is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that if you grasp an awl, since it has two threads, and the point in the thumb, and it makes pierce the left thumb as much as it has gone astray, so that the thread of the vein comes out at two fingers of the thumb; then extend the thumb from below to the whole awl, and the handle at one large spatulate.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb returns according to what is convenient, that is good; if not, take a saw and put it into the incision, and twist the limb, make two incisions or break through the bone in the middle of the limb; and let the two incisions be at two angles of the incision that you have made, or make one angle so that when they are assembled, the limb is as it is with a letter that does not have "I grieves"; then fix that bone, according to the quantity of its cost and swelling, of that which teaches the limb, then join the two separated parts, and bind them with a thread of silk; then cure this according to what we have said of the mollifying medicines and bands, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a fracture or sprain, or from cautery, then it is to be known that you must make a full incision of the hair with paper; and according to what has been said above; then remove between the two leaves of a book a tenth of an inch, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons will appear to be very learned in all sorts of things as to how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done in the work and the instruments in greater disposition.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the disease comes from a fracture or sprain, or from cautery, then it is to be known that you must make a full incision of the hair with paper; and according to what has been said above; then remove between the two leaves of a book a tenth of an inch, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons will appear to be very learned in all sorts of things as to how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done in the work and the instruments in greater disposition.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stiffness comes to the hands at home in a part like that in which the limb of the hand is soothed with oil white, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if it is to be known that you must bite the point of a scraper from the outside of the limb and hold it up; and extend as many times as necessary, until you have reached the part of the nail which is under the callous substance, which should not be too great nor too deep, so that the patient does not suffer from the callous too much and does not bleach the oil; and your incision, which you will make alongside that which is already assembled, must be slightly wider, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and all that is assembled must be secured, and no longer make any cuts in the oily water, but with soft water and vinegar; then put between the limb and the oil a tenth of an inch of linen, and put on the oil wool thickly in abundance; and after that use a little vinegar and other substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the oil of the unguent.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The unguent oil is of two kinds: one is nervous and somewhat dark in color, like pitch; the other is not nervous, but is like solidified moisture, and when touched with iron and warmed, it causes blisters. Both seem to begin to soften towards the great marrow, and spread throughout the body, covering the eyes and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And as for the method of the incision, if the patient puts his shoulder in its right place, then hold the eyes; then take hold of the oil with your hand, and grasp the hair with tweezers of small double curvature, and stretch it downwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle once and pierce the hair with the needle, and tie the hair with a thread and stretch it downwards, and drain at all times the surrounding area of the oil that surrounds the nail and the hair up to the root, and leave the natural discharge or secretion, if there is no crust of tears usually caused by the incision; and in no case should the oil be stretched only with the sponge and thread, as we have said; then the sponge should be wiped clean of the oil, which is the proper form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the spatula not touch the fleshy part and break it, and that the needle be not seen; and after the incision pour into the oil a little ball of burnt silk, and apply a compress of alum, and leave it until the other side; then cure what has happened as much as it is possible.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread will not pass, many times it is cured by this semblance of a medicine; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you see the oil of the patient, take the spatula lightly somewhat as I have shown you.</start_of_turn>
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail silently, and if you see that it has diminished somewhat and the edges are pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil compress of alum and red alum, and burn the silk, stamp the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work as I have said, until it is entirely healed.</start_of_turn>
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders thee in oil, as with a postulation of chaut, then milk, and first cure the postulation until it is healed, and then renew the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if there appears fat in the oil at night with great discomfort, if you suspend it on alum, and take a part and not the whole, that tears of tears do not arise; then distil in the red oil of the coleyer, which is made of litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the mark that comes on the plumule
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you temper the treatment with a weak oil from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not move your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	Des voines des eulz.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red which are covered with oil, and endure the weight of work and unburden the oil throughout the days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The master must first look at the oil, for it is strong, and there is no other disease fierce than this; therefore the master must command the patient to put his head in order, and then suspend the veins throughout their length as he knows how, and be double-folded in this fashion:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be double-folded by degrees in one fourth of an inch according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And bind them loosely with thread in fourths of an inch according to this form: then draw out the forces of those veins silently, and wipe away the blood hour after hour until you see that those veins have been freed from the oil; and make sure that you do not burn the oil with the spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and keep your mouth open in your work if you do not wish to faint from the heat. And when you have done this, if there is anything remaining that is still clotted, distill in the green and red oil to corrupt that which remains doubtful.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of this in that hour, make a plaster over the oil of soothing things that will calm the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and is assured to be relieved; and then begin again in the same way as before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	And if you cannot collect all of this in that hour, make a plaster over the oil of soothing things that will calm the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and is assured to be relieved; and then begin again in the same way as before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces from the fistula of the oil.

The mire so-called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine with burning water as I have said before, and it is not completely healed, if there is remaining moisture in it, you must make an incision over the abscess, leave it open, and drain out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, you will see the corruption and blackness, if the wound has all the instruments of the body; and is called "aspire chief", and is made with fine iron like a chisel when it is in this form.

And put upon the limb the corrupted bone, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand as much as you sense that that corruption is resealed; and do this never, then restore the limb of drying medicines.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is swollen, and there is pus in it, and the skin of the limb is swollen, and remains so for forty days, and does not heal and is not post-treated, and other bad things do not come, except to bring the fistula to the surface as it is; and uncover from the bone the second time by iron, and by strong medicines, and when it has been uncovered take hold of the fistula according to this fashion, and the angle of the iron should be at three angles, and the flesh should be thinned as much as you see here:

When the limb is completely open without any displacement of the marrow, without any relief, if you must bind the patient; then do the same, put on bandages or a dressing to absorb, then put on oil. de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This ailment called "alcunnati" is not fierce but appears in oil, resembling descending ice, and it is not actually ice; and the manner in which it appears is that if you make the patient sit on a chair that appears upright and straight, and take hold of his head between your hands two parts, and move him until you see the ice coming down to your eyes; then either bind it, do not let it descend, or break the light, and the patient will see things as if he saw before; and if it does not descend by itself, it is like acute pain, and if it descends again, the ice does not appear as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and place it upon the cornea; and hold it in place by continuing the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the brow quivers; and when it comes out, distillate in warm aqua mellea with honey, or in vinegar or fenugreek is boiled with honey, then be cured of another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the belly of the oil bowl.

se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the patient feels the pain increasing now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.

Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda does not manage to enter the oil because there are parts of the limb that have too tough hair, then you must take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the limb subtle, then I put in the cushion, as we have said; and when the work is finished appears to the patient the attendant coming behind, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark; and let him have no movement, and take light nourishment, and do not move his head to the left or to the right, and bind him as he pleases until seven days; and do not do anything else until the cure is finished or after the incision now, but make sure you feed him, because the pain will rise very quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do new or old ladies of various ranks appear, for there are some who seem like scorpions at the mouth of a piece; and if there are such or if they have hair entangled with hair of a reddish color, or if they have hair of a pale bone color.</start_of_turn>
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cases where there is pale hair which does not tangle, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and cover his nose, and spit on those hairs, and throw away the mucus; for it is better to support the subtle gut from one side, while you know that that hair is entirely bony.</start_of_turn
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains, if the wound has all its edges loose, if nothing stays in place; and if without support it breaks away, or is undermined, or if it is an abscess, then take hold of it as you would with a burn; and if it is malignant, burn it away as quickly as possible until it is quite black, and leave the charred parts untouched.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he does not move, and moisture comes up to the palate, saliva that he is sane; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, saliva that there is hair newly born in the bones above, because the instruments do not come down to the root: therefore it is necessary that you put in one thread of linen a little thick, and hold it with your hands, and leave between each knot no space at all or less; and put the patient’s hand under the thread at the end, and stretch until it comes out through the mouth; and often do the children do this, and it is a light thing for one who has seen it done; then take the fist that comes out through the mouth with one hand, and the other fist that comes out through the nose with the other hand, and bite the one after the other as we are or as the thread is.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Or of silver or gold, resembling a large coin, if like a chain; and guide it thus. de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the arm a disease which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes great at its outset, so that it is visible to the eye; and for this reason it is necessary that you immediately compress at the beginning, and break the bone, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you wait too long to compress it when it is great, if you take hold of it too tightly, it causes great pain to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of great color, you can easily bring it under control, if you empty the patient and compress it without fear, and cure the limb with dry things that restrain.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound together
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do not do that while the continuation is in its cartillages, for in many homes it has been found to be harmful.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it be for naught, if you see that the wound is fresh throughout its entirety; then join the two layers to a staple, and hold until it is healed. And if the layers are already separated at one end and the other, if you must pull out all the edges around the circumference until they are level, then reassemble the two layers to a staple, and strain, and sprinkle upon it powder of dragon’s blood and incense. Then place upon the powder a piece of dressing of great or other dressing that will adhere, and leave until it bleeds by itself, then cure when healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the costure is that you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said concerning the costure of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	from the incisions of the layers
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of the home, there are veins apposed like sharp grains of wheat, smaller and greater; therefore it is necessary that you return the veins, and make incisions above each knot, and grasp with tweezers and compress in the middle part; then employ the blunt end of the needle after making the incision of the vitriole, until it is no longer stained; and then withdraw the needle easily, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the hardness of the jaw bones.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens on the gums of the teeth that they become loose and the old people call them “albules”; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or blood clot; then take out the blunt end of the needle, or other astringent and drying powders; and if the gum comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	When the teeth are assembled at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are loose and rough; never are the teeth black and yellow and towards the front, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if you make the patient sit between your hands, and their shoulders are against your chest, and open the jaws or the gums split open, until nothing remains; and thus do you make blackening and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if you remove what is at the root at the first attempt, that is good; if that is not the case, if you must repeat the second and third time, until you have everything back in place; and the teeth that have been between the jaws must have various shapes because those that you remove to drive out the teeth have other shapes than those that are left between the teeth; and these shapes and others appear to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait a while before retracting too much, because it must not be made to move too much; because it is a high-quality substance, so we have no excuse for retracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that he will not suffer further.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient endures, and care must be taken that it is neither too great nor too little, and that it should be administered with care; and although it does not always depart with the pain, while the malady persists, for we have already wished to make these cures; and when you are certain that it will not do harm, if you must pull out the tooth entirely, then grasp the tooth firmly to ward off the gums from all parts; then bite firmly on the thumbs or hold with the fingers at the first joint, until they are well embedded, and then secure them firmly; and let the patient’s pain cease between the knees, and hold firmly if it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After is stretched out the tooth upright, and if it does not spring up, take none of these instruments and pull it out through a smaller hole, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the root is pierced and softened, if you can, cover it with bandages, or extract it; and if you grasp it too tightly, do not break it while grasping; and must cautiously move over the gum around the tooth with a scraper.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care well that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with greater pain than at first.</start_of_turn
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware that you do not act carelessly as the ignorant layman, who often break bones without any consequence, and bring no benefit to anyone except for our teaching; but they cause many to die from serious illnesses caused by roots that remain lodged, or by fractured bones, as we have often seen; and when the root is drawn out, cleanse the wound with wine or vinegar and oil, and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply a bandage of vitriol; and if this does not suffice, cauterize it.</start_of_turn
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, forasmuch as they are mute at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double when you draw the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when you draw, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so as to hold securely.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains lodged at the back, if you command that I take out the wet cotton ball inside, I shall do so immediately.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is pale, for in it are held the nails that are called “algrip,” for in this way the head of the shoulder appears like a beak of a bird; and they must be filed in the same way as with a file, and this is the form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not yield to all these tensions, if you must, uncover the flesh entirely around the root and place the instrument which is called “althali,” that is to say, a palainche, for this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If force and bulk are not sufficient to break me, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, if you assist with all your instruments, for when the forms come they will follow.</start_of_turn>
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has just rained, for this is its form:</start_of_turn>
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let there be great and firm grasps to hold the bone, so that it cannot slip but can be held and moved; and then restore the limb with the appropriate medicine for this case, and if there is any fracture in the bone, even if it is small, if the grasp has held all the instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural course, and the shape is deformed, even in female patients, if it is suspected that the tooth has penetrated too deeply and is not properly aligned, and cannot be remedied: then it must be extracted. And if it is affected with the tooth, if you take hold of this instrument which has the shape of a small beak, resembling a file, and is made of iron without a cutting edge at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And you must hold the tooth firmly in the palms of your hands for the duration of the tooth’s extraction, and because of that do not move the others, and if it appears, you can limber it, if you file it with a file that has the same shape as this.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is just like when we file nails; and while you are filing the tooth firmly in the palms of your hands, slightly move it until it stops bleeding; then at the end there is no rasping, and if it has penetrated too deeply and it bleeds the tongue, if you limber the root as much as it is necessary, so that it does not bleed or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are loose, whether by percussion or by pressure, and the patient cannot press against anything that would make it bleed, and you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is of no use; if you command to restrain them with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and softens, but the blood does not move; and let the wire neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth moving, if you take hold of the wire and pass it double between the two front teeth, then put the head of the shoulder between the teeth that are next to each other, as many as there are, until you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and steadily, until it does not move; and let your thread be fixed to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the arm with two pinscers, assemble them, and place them between the teeth of the jaw; and hold them in place so that they do not slip; and leave them in place until they can remain without support, for if they slip or the pinscer breaks, if strained by another thread; if it remains and serves its purpose, this is the form of a tooth and the figure of the arrangement of the two front teeth, and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you reset it in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let no other be between who is wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of ivory, and put it in its place or where the fault is, and strain it as we have said, and leave it so for a long time with constant tension
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this thread that comes from the tongue or the nature of the tooth absent from its place at birth; or by the accidental wounding of a deep wound; for the work is such that you must cover the mouth of the patient, and take hold of his tongue; then grasp the large nerve, until the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is pain or not, and this is the sign of a wound, if it comes loose and grasps the thread; and keep that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that comes from it; and when you have done this, if you raise the pale and easy blood, or cold blood, and put the tongue back in, and bind the patient tightly, that the wound does not clot.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes from a wound, take out the clotted blood with the forceps; and if it does not go away, burn it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	The tongue hangs limp and loose,
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes blood comes from the throat, which is called "godath", and it has two almond-shaped glands at the root; and when you treat them, as we have said in the preceding section, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and with a yellow-brown colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it, for if you do not, it will break by itself; and if it is pale in colour and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover, look first whether the abscess has settled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fais seoir le patient devant le soleil, ses bras soit en ton sain, et il serre la bouche et prend les serjans entre ses mains, et presse la langue vers le bas contre tout l’instrument, de sorte qu’il adopte la forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi comme un couteau.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press his tongue down with all your might, as this is the form; and let it be of silver or lead as thin as a knife.  See the boil, if you see it, grasp the poultice and insert it into the abscess, and push it out further than you can. And do not take away any cloth from there, then cover the instrument with the thumb, as this is the form, that looks like a force; and when the chief is bent, one place over the other, and is very sore, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can hold the teeth firmly, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can hold the teeth firmly, know that this is the form:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	Then make the patient sit before the sun, with arms at his sides, and grasp the mouth and grasp the serjeants between his hands, and press the tongue downwards against all the instruments, so that it takes the shape; and either of silver or gold subtle like a knife.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so big that it had forced two grains through two holes without pain.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had done so much, and remained alone in one place, and the traitor fled away, and took away a great portion of my bow; then I returned another part to the other side where I did not want it, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I returned the index finger to those wounds, and closed up a part, and only a little blood escaped; and as I was going to draw the conductor of the throat, the woman began to drink water and wine, and did not stop spitting from that wound until it became large; so I bound and cauterized it within the throat: since then I have had no sense of crossing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to me after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb hangs downwards, and it is fleeing and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure brings no benefit, and you see that the postulations are appeased, and it is subtle, so you must avoid the incision. And that which is rounded and assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of a yellow or black colour, so you must eschew the incision of the latter.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	You must therefore, when you see it, as I have said, from its redness and its length, that you make the patient sit in the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke before; then put on the ointment and drain, and hold for two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be known that you must not cover more than the superfluous that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, you will grieve the voice and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two thumbs, and cure as much as it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, it must be known that you must use an instrument at the cautery in the painful area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery if it is acute is harsh and fiery

Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. li chapistres des apostemes	the physician of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The seeds of an abscess are, according to what is remembered in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which they appear, one of which is in their own likeness and the other of which is due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for loose joints or when they are stiff.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the swelling of the limb is different from that which comes in joints, and the bones have their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if the swelling persists, one must not pierce it until the swelling has subsided according to its completion; and if there are those who must pierce it when it is hardened, and they do not subside according to their completion, as with swelling which is beside joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when the swelling comes from the joints, and it is left as it is until it is resolved, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When an abscess is perforated too late, if it be near the principal part of the limb; or if it be at the root, if it be pierced too deeply; one must only pierce the abscess in the normal course of digestion, unless it be at the root, that it does not split into two, and be prolonged, and there will arise a fistula; and it will not heal in a great length of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It must be known that you must wash the opening of the fistula that is dead according to its completion, when the pain is calmed, the departure of fever, and the fading of pain and redness, and the cessation of shivering and the burning of the fistula, and other signs; and it must be known that you must keep the opening or more dependent from the fistula, and the place where it is open. And let the opening be long enough for the bone or if the fistula is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and for all the bones that are equal or that have no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the situation of the limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is close to a callous bone, if it is worth mentioning that you must leave the perforation confirmed in the normal course of digestion, as we have said

en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.
