Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if thou dost close the vein or artery, and this doth thee not permit to work, if thou put in the wound a bit of vitriol broth, or some powders which remain bloodless, and restrain the wound; and let it alone until the swelling has subsided and the wound is softened, and then commence to move.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the swelling is gone, if thou returnest to thy work until thou hast completed it; then if thou must mark an index, if there remain no little scrofules, if thou dost cope and crush them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is in the root of the swelling a great vein, if thou canst not bear but to cope that swelling in its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging loose; then apply a bandage of white cotton pressed with Egyptian balsam, and then cure it
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you remove all the boils, if you are sure that you have reassembled the two layers of the wound, and you sew them now, there will be no remaining excess due to the size of the boils.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you are sure that you have grasped the root of the vein, and that you have tied it off, and you sew it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The boils which hold excess [fluid], pierce them or they will burst and die; and pierce them as before was said, depending on the matter, and mix attempts with ointment and similar things, so that it corrects what has been corrupted; and when the wound is well closed, if the ointment cure that which remains of the corruption, as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
de squinance	And if you cauterize the clot, if you dare to unite the four limbs of the wound and bind them now, and there is no longer any surplus due to the greatness of the clot; if you understand to cover the root of the vein, and to draw out the foreign matter, and to bind it as we have said. Those clots that hold surplus, pierce them through or they will open death; and pierce in the same way as the one said before, depending on the case, and mix with sponges and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well drained, if you apply an ointment dressing covering the scar, as long as it is healthy.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient men spoke of the size of the gorge; but I have never seen it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who are quarrelsome, it is necessary that the epiglottis, which is called the " epiglottis," be freed; and this will not help, for all the veins and the blood vessels of the patient are at those who have placed their faith above in the mouth, in the throat or in the almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the chest of the vomiting, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when our wings break the epiglottis, to cut them three circles or four, a little cut through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut through the cartilage; and if the blood vessel is close to the epiglottis, there must be no clot, and the blood vessels are long enough.</start_of_turn
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the master is fearful, if he commands that the skin of the throat be stretched to the chin, then cut the vein as far as the nail; and avoid the blood vessels, for if you see nothing, and then close the vein as we have said; and prove by the section of the smoke of the nail that the blood spurted out from the broken bone, and by the hoarseness of the voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and doubt of strangulation exists, unite the edges of the wound together with sutures, and bind them all around the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause the growth of flesh, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The Albucasim does this only when the throat is entirely filled, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default is abandoned.</start_of_turn
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, close the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound; and thus is kept from death; and for this reason the ancients command that the wound be left open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And then they command that the wound be sutured and healed, until it is healed; and I shall tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a damsel take a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut a part of her gullet; and I fled called for help, and found her just like she was dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had escaped from it, and saw that it had not pierced any vein or artery except for the throat, and the blood had come out through the wound.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and dressed the wound, and cured it until it healed; and the damsel did not feel any pain, and returned to her usual self; for in the cutting of the epiglottis I did not see any fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "neck hernia," and are great abscesses of the color of butter, and are much in women; and there are two ways of them: natural, and accidental. The natural kind has no cause
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is said to be of two kinds: one is like butter that has solidified, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one cannot safely perform surgery except in a small area, and the surgeon and attendants must be wary of all the surrounding parts: if you find it just like butter that has solidified, and cannot be bled from any vein, if you prick it, as we prick our fingers, and pull out all the contents, if there is none; and encircle everything well and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed
des nous	And encircle all around, and treat as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods exist for us, of which I shall speak of all; and know that I shall tell of all the difference that exists between a wound and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is caused by heat and fever that persists, as long as the swelling has not subsided, and is accompanied by pain; therefore rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With neither wound nor fever nor pain, it contains I syfac, which is its own sac and is of the color of burnt gold, and begins like wax and becomes thick; and they are like grains or grease or moisture, and the colour is such as I have said in the division
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, to inquire and examine first the instrument which is called the "entromissoire", according to its shape or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for inquiring about abscesses is that you take more moisture than you find in the abscess, and twist your two thumbs and two little fingers, until you know that the instrument has grasped the knot; then that it is done according to the size of the abscess; then draw out the entraume and be careful that the spur does not burst
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes too close, color it as you will; for if afterwards the interosseous membrane does not bring moisture, if it is fat, do then cross it, and grasp it with your fingers, and burn it lightly from the outer side and ward off the coat where you will treat it sound with the thumb; and if you do not treat it sound, tear it out piecemeal until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, if it returns to us many times; and if some remains, without grief, if you use for the wound some corrosive powders of vinegar, hold the wound tight, and put on soothing things around the wound, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if it is great, cut out two fingers of the wound, and treat it of that which engenders pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If the vein swells up against you or if it is another thing that makes you haste, and if you apply to it a little vitriol powder that has been ground, and leave it for three or four days, until the wound has closed, and rest the swelling of blood; then come back and do what is necessary to make it disappear.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the entromittent instruments, and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small; and there are three quarters which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, to embrace the fistules; and they are like needles which we sew the sores with, and they are made of saffron, or iron, or silver, and sometimes gold which is yellow, and are more proven for black blotches to embrace the cortices of fistules; and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the needles are like pieces of various appearances, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and for needles which have two cortices there are three kinds; and for needles which have three cortices, there are also three kinds; and for needles which have two cortices and a single cortex, there are three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of the humerus is broken and from such fractures there are some that do not pierce the skin but only one side, on which we must support the limb, for otherwise the vein and nerve are ruptured; and these interferences are the nails which are placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and they are not used for any other fracture than in the arm, leg, and elbow, and shoulder and collarbone, and similar bones; and no other instrument is ever used except for the nails, resembling the handles of fists, according to this fashion, because in this way we staunch the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he must never be placed in a place where he has previously grasped veins, arteries, or anything similar to that in form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Under no circumstances do the bones of the limbs of certain patients swell when they begin to become corrupt, so that they appear like female breasts; and they lie still and limp, and anyone who sees them will consider them cured, if they are bandaged according to this fashion from line b to g inclusive.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis. de la routure de l’artere	of the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is obstructed, and the skin is swollen which is above, if there are many abscesses there, and also comes out the vein above and abscesses; and if the surgeon knows when this is from the artery, when the abscesses are long and burst; and when he feels it in his hands, when he feels the extraction; and when it is from the vein, when it is reabsorbed downwards broken. And this is folly to cover this abscess, just as when it is swollen with boils and boils and spleen or in other parts, it is great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to discard the cautery of fire, and he who is at the head must also discard it, and in that which there is swelling of an artery that has been made known by the skin being long; then uncover the artery from its tissues, as long as it is covered; then take out an awl, and pierce it until the other side, and tighten the artery with two threads, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then hold the place that is between the two links of an intro-spiral until there is no more of it there, and bind the abscess; then administer the cure that is required, until it is healed; and if the abscess is of the size of a vein, it is necessary that you hold your hand in that way that you can make the abscess with all the skin, then take out the awl that you held in your hand, and pierce it, and there will be two threads, so that you can handle it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have said, or bind two threads of the two sides of the abscess with two threads; and if you doubt that the threads will hold, insert another awl at all the threads from the incision of the first awl, and tighten the threads to three threads; then cut the abscess as much as it is necessary, cut the excess of the tissue and leave only that which is bound; then put on a wet drape in wine and oil, and administer treatments of tentes and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Des apostemes des ners.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As with a wound comes an embolism in the vein or artery, comes an embolism as a nerve when it is irritated, or by too great a labour, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens with adjudiers and two musts and their limbs or if there are joints, and it is in great pain after incisions; and its color seems like the color of raw flesh, and is in many situations painful. And when it is strained, if it feels pain, it is not like the color of raw flesh, but like black bile; and it mutters loudly from all sides, neither going forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and he who is in joints does not cover himself with iron: by chance there is contraction; and he who is head or front, makes the skin taut at the staple.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the incision is small, if he has one nail, grasp it at the root; and if it is large, if he hangs it on the bone, and pulls, then bone and reunite the wound at the suture, and cure as long as it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	From the armpits downwards.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never has it been seen in the belly and nowhere else, and is a disease which is called "funge" because of its resemblance to grapes, and its root is subtle, and its head is large; and there are many small and great spots. I have known of two bellies which appeared more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were split open, and corrected themselves with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw two of them weighing eighteen ounces and six pounds respectively; and in the incision it was seen that the patient was moist, and the color of the artery was pale and moist with a thick root; if the bladder is large and the patient is present, apply the fire cautery to the fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the shoulder comes often too great a discharge of blood, and if it does not stop, if you are hasty, then do thou burn; and if you see the patient fainting and fearful from the incision of the flesh, if you take a thread of silk well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then the restraint, and do not cease to drain the thread of silk until it has closed the artery, and do the work by that; and if the roots are large, if there is fear of a fracture through the belly, but thou must well bind half, then burn that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that thou cover only the bulge which is of soft colour and of poor sense and of milk-regurgitation.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is fierce.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling comes from a burn or cut of the flesh, and is on the belly and there are some bowel movements, as is the case in other routes, or blood that has clotted in veins or arteries according to what is before, or from vomiting; and if it is through the rectum and through the outlet of the bowel, if it is the colour of the abscess, it is a light matter of pain, and has various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when one presses it there, if it returns and comes back, and by chance if it is caught, and brings forth much blood at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is an easy matter; open it well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain me; and if it is due to blood, if it is opened by these signs, the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed in quantity; and if it is due to wind, if it is stiff at the touch, and the work if it is that you see that it is due to the blood of an artery or a vein, or the wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you think that you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or as the chapter says, concerning the abscess of the artery or the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If it appears to be the intestine or the boil, command the patient to keep his hand steady, and if it is prolonged to the right, then mark it down at the edge of the wound; then order him to move his hand between your hands, then bring his thumb to the middle of the wound, and extend half of the abscess downwards over the entire breadth; then bind it with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and leave it in place; then cover half of the abscess extending above the thread, and put your index finger and the intestine together; if you find the intestine caught in the thread, if you pull it out, bring the intestine out from under the belly; if you find the boil, if you grasp it at the head, and cut off the excess; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, if it comes together, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have done in the shape that you think you have pierced; then strain the abscess for three days on the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it swells, and cut off the dead tissue by itself; or you can drain it when it has gone down and swollen, then cure the wound of what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and suture the limb.</start_of_turn>
dou chancre	Then strain the abscess for three days on the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the liquid alone until it bursts by itself; cut off the dead flesh by itself.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said concerning the appearance of carbuncles, how one must work upon them with medicines, and how one must shun the cautery; and we say that carbuncles fester in marshes, and cause great pain in their cure. The ancients say that when carbuncles are in their prime or can be scraped out like those which are in mammels, and in the gut, and in similar places, one must remove them at their commencement; and when they are great and old, if one cannot approach them, for I know of no remedy for them; nor have I ever seen any healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the work is in its prime or can be scraped out as we have said, do not purge the black bile from the patient at any time; then make the patient healthy if he has shown repletion, then expel the patient. i.e. give him good liquid to make the work. Then remove nails or carbuncles, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts round about; and let the blood flow freely, and keep your hand or any other thing away from it, and if the wound is closed from the artery or vein, do not cauterize more than is absolutely necessary; then treat with another cure until he is healed.</start_of_turn>
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	You have said in division that the signs of hydrophobia are seen when water is assembled, and the signs of spleen resemble those of chescune, and the treatment for the former is by medicine, while for the latter by iron: if only the light is eclipes; do not touch iron in these two signs, that is to say, tympanites and iposarche, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when medicine is taken for this sign which is called "eclipses" of medicine, and the treatment does not profit, if you observe that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides hydrophobia, as in most cases and solution of the belly and other things; do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great vigor and there is only hydrophobia, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work: take hold of the patient with your hands, and the assistant shall press the abdomen at the lowest point of the water, and then take the spine in this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let two parts suffice.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let two parts suffice. When the wound has reached two parts, and all the rest does not protrude more than to the intestines when it is grasped, and does not bleed; then look if the hydrophobia is leaning towards the intestines: if it seems that it is in the spleen, if you make an incision three fingers breadth to the left of the spleen; and if it is from the disease of the liver, if you make an incision to the left of the spleen; and if it is from the bile, if you make an incision to the right, and do not let the patient rest on the incision except for the slight tremor of an nail or as much as when you are scraping off a nail; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and extract the spleen, and keep your hand over the wound with all your might between the skin and the bone as if you were grasping the quantity of a nail or as much as when you are scraping off a nail; then pierce the bone until the tremor ceases. This is the way the instrument should be held.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver dollar, with a vein or an archway at the top; and on one side there are one small hole and three holes on the other side, and two on the other; and the head of the shoulder is cut off like a quill, and this is the form of the incision which the writer makes to cut off the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	The head of the sufferer is the stake, if when the instruments come into the water, if they are now resting on the instrument, it is necessary to remove half or a third of the water; for if you remove more than that, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit of the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death; but remove according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to the injunctions of the virtue of the patient himself, and his wounds; then take away the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the cork which is stamping the hole which is above the socket, as I have said; that you pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering in this way, and take away a small quantity of water; do this under no circumstances, and keep it until it stops being a matter of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if thou doubtest of the patient, and thou seest him mouthing with pain, if the physician doth cure by burying or washing with sand the caulker, and by mouthing with sweat or bath and sun, and if thou dost observe him to drink; and if the physician doth give him drying medicines until he be healed, and doth cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the extraction of the pain, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do this to no man, and guard yourself from using it until it ceases to linger; for if you doubt the patient, and you put too much water in, if the cure be of the burying of earth or sand, with water or sweat, and by the sun, and drink wine; and take drying medicines, until he is cured, and cauterize upon the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born who have not a mark in the belly, or the mark is small, or it is not well placed in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If he coves so much that he cannot perceive at all all the surrounding things according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put or prick the clot of blood of the loin, and bind and hold it for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if he keeps it closed, he will urinate, and then put it back; and by chance it will not be able to stay closed, because the urine which comes out will not leave it closed.</start_of_turn>
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	When the opening is small, if medicine is applied with a lead weight, as we have said, and it expands.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	When they have not recently had the opening in their limb, they are black because none are born with the opening at the head of the bone, for they cannot urinate before they lift up their thigh; and they cannot urinate because the material cannot come down to the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies recumbent on his back, and the head of the bone and the hip are as wide as a thumb, if the opening is in the middle, as it is right; you must prevent excessive bleeding that comes often, and if it comes, if the discharge of that which discharges blood is stinted, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des pustules de la verge	of boils of the hip.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils onto the limb, and are an appearance of foul matter; and in them there are both malignant and benign ones; if you take them at their root, anoint them subtly, and evacuate them all out, then put on a wet cotton dressing in Egyptian fashion; then cure them with diafinicon until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the swelling is malignant, of dark colour and purulent, it is necessary to bring cautery there.

When you have grasped it, and if the swelling is at the root of the thigh, and has some inside the bone and some outside, you must first break the swelling that is inside; and when it is broken, if the wound is outside
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure them altogether, if you do not firmly secure the shoulder, black bile and corruption will arise in its marrow and bone; if you remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and sometimes, cure them of other diseases until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood clots come away, if you mix the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two situations: that of blood clots and of corruption; and if the head of the bone is corrupted and withdrawn, if you swallow or force out a clot of blood, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has fallen out at the root of the bone which has not been circumcised, or if there is pain or incision, if you then burn it with the instrument which severs, until the ligaments are loosened, and deliver the head of the bone from all parts; and if this causes division of the limb, if you then burn it at the tip of the bone and the nail; then dry thoroughly between two, and put on a bandage of fine linen moistened with cold water, which does not adhere.
de la circoncision	If it is urgent to divide this, if you must, then cover the head of the limb with a cloth without any hair or nail; then slowly separate between two joints and put a wet linen bandage on with cold water, so that it does not slip
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply a continuation of the ailment if like other wounds; however, since we are doing this work of our own free will, and properly undertake it, if it is necessary that we do it better, and the milder way for the health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old doctors did not teach me circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision to make a hole, and to force, and with all their skill; yet if the testicles escaped because there were two threads, and by chance if one sews up the lower and leaves the upper unsewn.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound closes again, and the pain is doubled, and there is swelling which is more than just a little discomfort; and by chance the thread escapes, and corrects the work, and many times comes out without there having been any need for it, and I have seen that.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made by force throughout the whole length of the thread, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces tear just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equal all around in height, but the thread is well stretched over the leather; and the manner of the first work is that if you make the child think, if he understands, do not make him force the thread through the hole only as much as is necessary, but pass it through in all the ways that you can; then pass the thread between your hands straight, and return the forces between your hands or remove your fingers from those which the child cannot see, neither any of the instruments; then take hold of your hand at the wrist and blow or call, and draw it up as high as the head of the bone is extended; then move it well from the dirt that is assembled, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it again from one side to the other; and hold for two minutes by the second loop to the pouch and the index finger, and press between the two loops, then leave the callus down slowly and draw out the head of the bone; then leave the blood to flow freely, and put powder on and over the powder a bandage glued with a piece of rosewater seed which has been ground up with oil of rosebud and balsam, and leave it until the next morning, and treat in like manner until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	If the force of the limb is weakened in this way: let the two shoulders be tense and taut, and let the limb be as strong as the hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the limb is when the nerves are injured during the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your finger, even though it makes an incision; and hold it equally, and if you do not manage to hold your finger, if you keep it tense, and then let go.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass two days, and what is beside the navel is inflamed, if you leave them as long as the afterbirth is quiet, and the swelling is slight; if you touch them as you wish, and hold onto the navel, it will do you no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you touch too much powder to a wound, as we have said, or treat it with powders, and you touch it more than enough, and it swells up, if it does not heal; cure it as we have said before, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	Regarding the retention of urine...
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or blood clot, or bowel, or a worm, or other things, which we have mentioned in the previous division; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the obstruction is caused by the stone which is inside the kidney or the neck of the bladder, if it is suspected that the patient is bent over his knees; and let him place his feet outside the back, and extend his belly from the part below his back, and restrain the patient so that he does not move as much as he can; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is freed; and if it does not come, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, if it is suspected that there is an instrument which is called the "siringue," which is like this: either of silver with a narrow neck like a bird's beak; or the caine of a palm half-grown; or like the beak of a sparrow.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus it is with the issue of urine: if you take a pair of fine needles and bind one to the head of a wool or cotton swab, and pass the needle through the bladder; and squeeze out the excess wool and pass until it reaches the head of the bladder, then join the bladder with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and raise the bladder and the oily parts with oil of olive and tepid water; then gently insert the bladder into the vagina, until it reaches the root of the vagina, then double the vagina backwards against the pubic bone; then withdraw the bladder forward until it reaches the bladder, and make the patient feel the urine coming until it reaches the empty state, for this is not done except in this order because of what it brings or what it goes with; then draw out the needle at both ends, and the urine follows the thread, and withdraw the needle again, and correct the urine; and do it again until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are stones or blood in the bladder, or if pus is accumulated, and you see urine and medicines boiling over, if you do everything that is called the "clepsedre," which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if there are three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine can be forced down as well as possible, if we can manage to drive out the moisture, and push strongly as necessary; and when you see the medicine vomiting in the bladder, put the head of the sufferer over the moisture, and drive out the one who is fainting. If you drive out the moisture from the sufferer, and then push strongly again, if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder, the patient will feel it; and this is the form of a subtle cluster from which we clusterize the bladder.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from I seam or the two bones meet; then take a bladder of a kid and put the moisture in which you see clustering the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a double bow, and burn I part of that moisture over the fire; then bring the head of the cluster to the verge, and strain your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make I circle, and pierce it round the edge; then pull out the thread strongly through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling I doll, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it up with the instrument; and do as you would with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division how to perform an incision of the stone, and the extraction with medicine; and we have mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that must be extracted; and in what case a stone must be opened by size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and concisely about them.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is retained in the bladder is oftener painful than when it is outside; and this is a sign that the bladder is suffering from excessive urine which resembles the suffering in its subtlety; and there is frequent straining, and the patient suffers great pain in his side, and he goes to the toilet many times, and then grows stiff; and from these strains the foundation is loosened.  And it is easy to cure these strains until they are three years old; and after that it is more difficult in old men, and is as bad in young men as in old; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, if it is necessary, we must first cleanse the patient by vomiting, to drive out all the poison that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never fails to require cutting into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move downward, until the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and let it never go too high; then make it sit between your hands, and put your hands on its thighs, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then touch and feel inside; if you feel the stone in the space, do it quickly and cut above the stone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not yield to the touch, put your left thumb on the belly, if the patient is elderly, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and press in its foundation, touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if the spleen is at the collar of the bladder; then press above your finger, and the stone will come out whether you see it or not
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder to his hand, and command him to extend to his right hand the ribs above, and to his left hand bone the skin which is below the ribs in the part where we make the incision; then put the sponge in covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between these two that are between the buttocks and the fundament, do not put it in the middle but at the cost of the left hip; and be right over the stone, and your two thighs must either be adducted or flexed, and be the size that it will traverse if it is wide enough, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, do not put it too large; for chance the press if you must put something over the stone that it leaps forward in its work; and the hair that is on the edge of the stone or that is angled, and margins: if it is hairy, grasp it to hold it; and if there is something soft there, it is like a gland, rounded, from which it issues lightly.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are angles and margins on it, make the size greater; and if it does not leap, it is certain that you must pull on the nails which are just like a file at the head, for the nail must be pulled out if it escapes; or you must grasp it with forceps at the head; and if you do not manage to grasp it, if it is loose, the opening will be large; and if it is not properly closed, it is like a burn from vitriol; and if there are several stones, pull out the largest at the belly of the bladder first, then close and then pull out the others.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is too large, if you cover it with a cloth, it makes a greater wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And if it is too large, if you cover it with a cloth, it makes a greater wound. For in this matter two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out with such force that the testicles cannot withstand it; but whatever you do, if you try to remove it by pieces, as long as you are doing so, until you have completed your work, if you employ incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and hold it tight, and put upon it a moist bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the burn; then restore the patient to his collar and do not loosen the knot until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, if there arises much pain like the smell of oil and water, then cure with ointment of diafinicon and ointment of basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if there are urine scalings in the wound and corrosion, and blood clots in the bladder, and either because of this the urine is retained, which is known in part as without a splash with the urine: take then your dose in the wound, and evacuate that blood, for if it remains, it will burst the bladder. Then wash the wound with water and easily and with silk, and give him aid in every way that you can, until he is healed; and know that all the times you treat him, bind the two edges together and assemble the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is either a tube or a passage from the bladder, and is fixed firmly, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician who is treating this should say thus, that you must many times, he will hear of the size of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already heard of this from someone
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the iron as described above and be at a right angle with two handles fixed at a distance of one thumb:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.
