Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bone is fractured, and a spur of urine comes forth with the urine, and the patient is in pain; if you are unable to do this by any other means, then take a thread and pass it through the hole of the stone and another through the other hole, and pass the string between the two lines, and then draw it out, and loosen the string, and solidify the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you are unable to do this, grasp the limb firmly by two fingers, and then place your thumb between the two fingers and grasp the limb at its base. Then pull the limb out forcefully, loosen the ligature, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the limb is dislocated in women, and if this never happens, if it is cured, it is defended by two things: the first is that sometimes the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to manage her household, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third method if by chance you cannot find a woman who is very skilled in this work of hands; and the fourth method if the woman’s stone is more prominent than the man’s, for it is capable of making a deeper cut, and great pain it has. And if it is necessary to do so, if you take a slight measure which is well knowing, and prick the trueve bone with a needle, and if you do not find it, do not cast aside the subtle measure; and present a dance well wise in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the work, and command her to do what you command of the inquiry of the stone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: for if she is, you must push her head or foundation and query the stone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her head from her head, and command her to hold her head or with the patient, and ask and press her left hand on the bladder forming.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she be true, if you must move her from groin to groin from the entrance of the bladder to the knee, as far as she comes to the root of the thigh; then clamp upon the thigh at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone there where it is usually seen, and feel the thigh in that part; and do not move her up or down the thigh or knee, and make her small at first; then tighten her up to the size, if you feel the thigh is swollen as much as the wound will bear, and that her thighs are like many other thighs: that is to say, small and large, round and square, long and round, and hairy.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if her thighs look like the others you will know she is cured.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if she does not go away, if you put in vinegar broth and hold it for an hour until she is dry; then return to your work, until the wound is healed, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the arrow as home to help you in your work; and if she does not go away, and it is the artery that is clamped, if you put powder on the wound and strain out clothes and bands, and do not begin again, and leave the wound alone and do not touch it, except by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the color of blood has subsided and the limb is relaxed, if it returns to its work, as long as the wound is still open.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is like lumps of wax, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not another act; and it is the skin of the egg between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this leech is from weakness that comes from the eggs, and it is spread through that substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes upon the bones, and this moisture is of many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are signs of congestion in this assembly, for if it is white or pale yellow as we have said, if the abscess is round like an egg, and does not open the bones, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a part of the yolk, and because of this it is thought that this is one egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white pith, if it feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it appears throughout the entire mass, as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, following the introducer, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we bind it with iron, if you command that the patient be calm and still, then lift it up on its back, upon something high, and put on it some thick cloth; then sit on its left side, and tell the minister to sit on its right, and extend the limb to the second rib from the navel of the coions; then take the sponge and wipe the skin of the coions among them from the navel down to below the navel; and make a straight incision dividing the skin of the coions up to the white spot, and burn it subtly as it comes; then pierce the white spot with water to I large opening, and drain all the water, and then put on your sponges, and raise the white spot; and do not touch the navel, but only the white spot; wipe all or in pieces immediately the cost of it subtly, for if you do not wipe it well enough, the water will return; and if the blood spurts out on your work, keep it in its place until you have finished the work of the white spot; then assemble the two leaves of the navel to a costure, and cure it as the others wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the jaw corrupted by another illness, you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut the bone throughout its suspension, drain the abscess, and cure it like we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is collected into two parts together, like two roots; if the other part is similarly shaped as you have made the first one, then dry the blood, and put in the wound a layer of lint soaked in rose oil; and put on another layer of lint soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two bones, and put under doubled cloths, and bind on all around as it is customary in this case.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool yarn as described above and be assembled by stitching in the armpit, and one of the bones grasps on the foundation up to the shoulder, and the other at the painful part; and the other two thumbs on the two angles, and when all is assembled, restore the restriction in the armpit loop; and never is this branch of cautery like the size of iron, and take only one needle burnish, and prick the skin of the bones, and if there is a white swelling that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the cautery as described above, and burn that swelling as we have said, and burn with this subtle burnish.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if you apply it in all ways as you wish, until you are satisfied; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and take that this work is more profitable; and observe that the works of this size are safer; and do not do anything that opposes, or incisions or other things that may harm, until you have cured what opposes.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horribleness, if he accepts perforation, as I have said, and when you are certain by the indications that the aqueous extract is sufficient, if you make the patient sit on a low chair; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with the whole of the surrounding area wide open, and make the perforation deep enough; and if the wound is large, make the opening wide enough for all the blood to drain out; then put a pad on the wound and bind it tightly, and leave the remaining blood to drain out naturally; and cure the wound until it is healed; and if the bleeding does not stop, drink a penny or the instrument used for treating the hydropic swelling, as it is formed above; and widen the wound and make sure the blood returns, and assemble it after six months or when the pain has ceased, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the heel of the foot.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Hares that in this section of this twig have doubt in many places, for I believe that moisture is worth leaving; and I shall tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come or break, and I have seen this often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive swelling and pain, which is spread as far as the joints; or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is like that of honey; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief; and sometimes it is a perforated abscess, full of pus and blood, of a reddish color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the disposition of the abscess that it is solid, when you touch it; and I do not believe that you should touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain in the thighs, and can well make the size above this semblance, and above the other limbs; and that you must keep close to the coions, then the egg is on high, and the thread is of white silk, and deliver the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cooked with these legs that are not needed, if you must therefore draw out the egg, and keep close; and if it is in the silk, or in that which is within the blood vessels, if you must deliver all that is within, and keep it rounded off.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage is loose at the root or behind, it is necessary that you grasp it all, and pull out the root, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you employ wool wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the heel of the foot.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering similar to an eye, with the softening of the coions, and the patient groans greatly when he moves; and the cure for this disease is very similar to that which we have said before, and all that we will tell you about this matter will be according to what the ancients have done
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on the left side of the chair, then suspend the ligature from the two hooks at the waist, to all the vessels that stretch to the groin, and hold them firmly, and stretch them out; then pierce through the thick membrane with a large needle to open the vessels, as much as they are uncovered, and then drain the pus from the wound, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert an awl or a double thread, and tie it to the first part or where the vein has come loose, and tie it firmly to the other part; then press firmly around the middle, according to the length of the bone, and remove the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or apply a bandage, so that no vessel leaks that nourishes any of the testicles; for by that there will be no harm, and if all the vessels come together, if you tie the testicles to all the vessels, if they do not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and dry and do not swell.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the disease
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The coming of this root is by section which comes from above or by extension upon the belly in the part of the intestines; for the intestines descend from that route to one of the buttocks; and that route is either by section or by extension of the root, and these two ways are the causes: either by percussion or by jump, or by pressure or by raising the grief weight, or by similar things; and the signs when it is by section of the syfac are that there is swelling and swelling in length, and that it does not come immediately; and the abscess is equal up to the navel, because the syfac presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the shoulder is dislocated, it causes sudden pain, and the scapula is displaced, from the stretching of the skin and the protrusion of the bone from the shoulder socket.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does blood flow with the intestines, and is retained when it is pressed, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, because it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient must retain the intestine in its place within the wound, if it can return there; then either sew on its collar between your hands, and hold the thighs; then place the thumb above, and grasp all the skin of the buttocks from the length; then push inwards the intestines to the size that you must do to open the wound, and so on; then pull out the syfac that is below the skin of the buttocks, as long as the white syfac is discovered throughout; then place your index finger in that which teaches the buttock, in that which is between the white syfac which is below the skin of the buttocks, and between the second syfac, and depart that which is behind the buttocks, and between the second syfac; and then move the hand of the wrist inwards of the buttock, and place the white syfac at the top of your left hand, and hold the buttocks to the whole syfac towards the size; and command the minister to extend the buttocks in high, and unfasten that which is behind the ligature; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or white syfac hardened, and if you find nothing, if the wound is at the back; then take a needle or make a large stitch of X threads, and pass it in the back part of the syfac, which is behind the skin of the buttocks; after the size, then grasp the threads that appear from the needle, until there are three threads; and assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and tie the syfac, which we have said is behind the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the threads with the skin, and tie them in two parts, so that no vessels that support them can enter into the wound, except for the wound itself; and put the thread back according to the first thread along two fingers; and after these two threads leave the syfac that is behind the buttock with a great space; and after all the rest according to the roundness of the egg. Then grasp at the part that is behind the skin of the buttocks, as much as without remorse, and bow; as we have said before; then mix coarse wool with oil, and put it in the wound, and mix the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the fat surrounding the wound as we mentioned before, after the incision, in doubt of further bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the limb stay still until it quiets down; and if it lingers too long, if so be raised from hot water, and put on what we have said, until it quiets down; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.

Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez. Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes rupture in anger, as we have said, and open the wound; and do not touch any intestines as they are connected, and if you do, that is enough, and repair all the hours; and all the blood that remains will depart; and this happens from the extension of the sinew that is in anger, as we have said, because it is extended, then is softened and relaxed and open; and cure it if by cautery, as we have said before; and never cured by iron in this manner: and let the patient lie still on his back between your hands, and grasp the limb of the rupture inflated with a large measure of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew that is under the leather that covers it, and take hold of the hair and bring it out from the swelling; and press down on the belly, and cut out the two ends of the sinew that appear from the swelling, and cut one and the other; and then draw out the root of the swelling, and do not cover up the swelling or extend the egg or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines; and cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you have closed the wound, if the swelling subsides and heals the wound, as long as it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no mark in its course, and the burn is mute in this place, and more adjacent to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times is the skin of the nails softened in households, because the nails that are within are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when you see it cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then gather the layers together with a staple, and if you see that, close the excess of softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the hair.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	That which chastens is commanded in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to force it except in two ways: one is that the witness to the wound responds when asked and gives the cure; and the other is that we often mix up the chastening of some beasts with our attendants, as with oxen and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastening is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one where we do it by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the joint is softened and limp; then we grasp it with our hand, until it is set and you can no longer feel it
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the shoulder joint: it is commanded that you hold the best position, and press the skin of the armpits to your left hand, then bind the sling, and support upon each side at the top of the shoulder when you have well supported them; and leave no trace of a scab or any secret matter which is on the vessels; and this method of cautery is more delicate than that which is done by traction, for in traction remains by chance no hair, for it desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, and for this reason I would rather not speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary for us to do so for two reasons: the first is that the patients themselves can respond when asked, and the second is that we have often had to cauterize beasts for our assistants, such as oxen and sheep and goats and others. I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.  In the former, we seat the beast in warm water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are firm and we can no longer feel them.  As for cauterization of great size: it is necessary to hold the beast steady, and to press the skin of the hairs with our left hand; then to bind the suspension, and to grasp each hair with our thumb and index finger, when they are well secured; and leave no trace of blood or clot on the vessels.  This method of cauterization is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction the beast desires to move; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways as at home: one is if between the two testicles there appears as much as the figure of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the navel as much as a phallus and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for wounds and boils is that you cover all the boils with lead plates; in the second method, for those whose urine spurts through the pores of the skin, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in accordance with two manners: one if between the two testicles opens as with the figure of female nature, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine of the female. And the other manner if it is in women, and has on the navel as with a girl and two testicles. And the cure for the tumour and fame is if you cut off all the testicle stones, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tension of a wound is a boil placed on the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have had as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to hold the superfluousness of the tension at your hand or armpit, and to grasp it lightly; and do not go too deep, for blood does not come out, then the cure of other medicines as long as it is healthy; and at another wound that arises at the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and that is called the old "coward disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you manage to keep it still, as we have said, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is erratic because the woman’s nature is not known, or if the rupture is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that comes with it; or it is caused by injury, or by a subtle or thick scab, and it is made by dirt, or gravel, or pus, or anything similar; and if it begets conception, and the birth, and by chance the flowers are to have; and the knowledge of this is by the regard of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling is close to the surface, if you wish at the shoulder or at the elbow.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle scab, and it is close to the skin, if you are in a hurry, and it bursts: put your two thumbs together, and the patient should be behind, with her legs spread; then the two thumbs are to be placed, as long as the subtle scab is round, and above the swelling; then take oil, and pour it on the wound, and put it on the limb, and lie the patient down on her chest, so that it does not swell further
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, it is recommended that you grasp it with pliers resembling a laurel leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of a hard nature, if you suspend it on the incision and grasp it; and have medicines at rest, such as chamomile, dragons blood, incense, and plenty of eggs; then mix in some lard, so that the wound does not adhere; and let it be long, and mix in some lint; then let it be cured by other means until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the marrow comes soft, if it is grasped according to this method, it will not be an abscess.</start_of_turn
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the marrow, do not touch fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	Des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without support are not usually cured, and when they are old if they become swollen; and we have mentioned in the preceding chapters the signs and symptoms, and I shall now say which are the ones which bring about cure
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	The ones which are at the bottom of the belly, we can sense them, are those which we can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the abscess tightly with your hands, and press on its roots, then sprinkle on soothing medicines like acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces when an hour has passed, and put it in cold water; and when the bleeding stops, if you wish, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then give her barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make I plaster on her back
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is swollen, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make a circular bandage at the back and have lumps towards the wound; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and make the wound air-tight.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the abscess rests, if you cure the limb of its swelling as long as it is healthy; the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a blackhead, if you cover it as I have said before; and then cure as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not accustomed; and when old, they become swollen; and as we have said in the division, their signs and symptoms, I will say here those which resolve cure. I say that emorroids and swellings, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the cure with iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the testicles tightly, grasp the head in its roots, then sprinkle over medicines which restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then put it into cold water; and if there is still bleeding, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take oatmeal, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one application upon her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is a wound at the back, and there are clots, take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make it bleed. And when the wound is healed, if it is a swelling which is called “albathir,” it is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the swelling; and then it will heal as well.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come about in the belly, such as carbuncles and pyreous abscesses and herpes and worms and tumors and fistulas and hemorrhoids and scalded abscesses, and other diseases which I have mentioned in the previous section.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is obvious that you are in great distress at this treatment of the carbuncle that appears in the armpit; for it is not of the common carbuncles that remain stuck; and if you are able to learn the work of iron, behold if the carbuncle is already in the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red as you see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not be in a hurry to pierce, but make me wait until the pain is gone; and then seat the patient on a chair, and take two small stools or a cushion and support him on his back and join his limbs together; and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his hands under his knees, and bind them securely with a bandage; then draw out the swelling towards the breastbone, and bring the instrument that we use to open the armpit, so that this thing comes into its natural shape; and know that when you bring this instrument, that you should first make a hole to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters under the instrument does not go too deep and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the armpit with a cloth so that the instrument does not hurt; and know that you must put the cap of the instrument under, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when an abscess ruptures, and one washes the hand with oil, if the clot covers the head, the spleen and the liver; and when the wound is emptied, one must put in the wound some soft wool soaked in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the dressing firmly over the wound, and put over it a layer of linen cloth soaked in water or mallow, which must be cooked; then one must cure the wound after two days of washing following this. As long as it is not healed, do not remove the dressing and the wound by force with water and honey, but with water or the root of rue and arnica, which must be cooked; and then repeat the washing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the wound, one must take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the previous part.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The peasant is first of all at the dance when he knows the figure of natural birth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down on her belly and desiring to smell the broth: then the child is immediately born; then the afterbirth that follows is like the natural figure of a birth, and the child comes out head first, and supports itself with its hand; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on her belly, the child will come out head first; for when it comes out head first, it supports itself with its hand, and the mother delivers the afterbirth of its superfluities by natural confinement. This is what comes not from nature but from the devil.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It never comes from its feet, but comes from the ribs or the shoulder, or the hands, or it comes from its belly or its side, and is converted by an accident from its collar, and by other harmful figures; if the peasant is at the dance and is wise and discreet in these matters, and avoids error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures in which one must help him
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child naturally descends on his navel, the woman gives a gentle push, and the child’s ability is weak; if she sits on a chair or the women hold her; and she should have an oily substance or rue to anoint herself, and then she should join the dance between her two thighs where she forms a small space.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and bind its nail as long as the moisture which is inside comes out; and press the belly of the woman as long as the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to clench the woman with muscle spasm of ruegen with oil of poppyseed; then make her drink and vomit violently, and keep her mouth and nose covered for an hour: if the fetus is now gone.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out violently, if you can, hold them lightly thus and thus; and if they will not enter, put the woman on a seat, and support her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the earth, and hold the woman, that she does not sneeze; and if the hands will not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you grip the hands at the shoulder which is in front, and pull out the fetus, and strain equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on his feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon his feet, if you can push upwards; then twist a little to the right and to the left, until they are even; then grasp the feet and extend them to the right and to the left.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he cannot jump up to the hips, if the master commands him to jump, and makes him cough; if he jumps up, God help him
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If not otherwise, if the limb hangs limp and limp, as is natural.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily done.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump up so willingly as we have seen, say if he takes muscle powder of elevation, and oil of poppies, and gum masticated, and grind them all together; and put on the nature of the woman inside and remove this swelling, then let her sit in hot water until the ribs are dry; and when she is softened up again, give her a collar of myrrh, and put on her clothes, and leave her for an hour; then let her sit on her seat, then make her cough and strain her mouth and nose, and take her pulse gently, for the child jumps now
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the child’s discharge from his genitals.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the boy comes in this shape, if he puts his hands on his face and chin; then either he is sleepy on his collar and hangs his head down, or he is asleep; and he folds his hands on his chest and then grasps his hands under his belly, and pulls up his buttocks as much as they appear from his throat; and if the boy does not jump, take his hands and move them, then move his belly upwards, and put back his hands; and the boy will yawn and stretch; and tell the woman to hold him until the boy is better.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child who comes out with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you to make the limb move: if it will not move, if you cannot lift the limb, call for help; if she cannot call for help, make her lie down on her side, and pull out the legs forward; then bring in the muscle that I told you about; and if she does not move, make her sit on the edge of the bed, and study to restore the limb; and when the limb is restored, the child will recover according to his natural figure, and make him cough, and command her to hold him until the child is better.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child on his neck, and his hands spread out, and his face twisted towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command thee to grasp his hand firmly, then rotate it forward and backward, and move it lightly; and when it is equal, place upon it the oily substance of alum and oil, as we have said, and then command it to move forward and backward; and when thou hast done this, command him to sit down and command him to grasp it; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same measure at all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes forth with force in this manner at every second, if thou grasp its finger, while the moisture is evacuated; and if it hangs upon his face and neck, grasp the abscess, that it be not retained, and the child will die; then draw the child inwards, as thou didst command, and command the woman not to touch it again: for it will be loosened lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	Therefore if it is slightly dislocated.

de l’enfant mort	De l’enfant mort.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or womb, if she does not suffer greatly, and you are constrained by the work of your hands; if you believe that the woman is in good health, and has no accident or fears of death; if you believe that the woman is lying on her back, with her shoulders flexed forward and her legs raised; and that the minister takes hold of two fingers, or binds her to the bed if she does not recover at the descent of the child; then smear the mouth of the woman with oil moistened with muscus of alum and fenugreek and poppy seed, then anoint her hands with these oils and these muscus; then put her in the basin lightly, and wait until she comes to or until she vomits what is convenient for her, and take care that the child descends from his head; if you put the sponges in his eyes or nose or in his mouth or in the palm of his hand or by the beard or in the forcele or close to the ribs, and if the descent is on his toes, he will grasp or bite and has low ribs; and take hold of the sponge with your right hand, and put the heel between the two of your left hand, and hold her firmly with your whole hand, and grasp the sponge in none of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the hook finds another bone, or the third one if you are dealing with it, if so the extraction must be even; and then stretch them evenly by moving from side to side, for that is the way to break, and if the nails are left in, keep them in place by means of force.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers. And if the head of the shoulder is great and swollen at its exit, or if there is much pain collected there, if you must stretch out the spinous process between your two thumbs and hold the pain and draw it out; or you must twist it with the instrument which is called the "almidach," as it comes with the instruments or chapter which follows this one; and thus make the swelling grow naturally; and then force out the bones as they hold them, and if the head of the shoulder leaps out and strains at the forcele, if it is split, as much as the moisture that comes out; and if it cannot be closed, if the cavity fills with pieces of bone as you must; and if it is swollen in the belly or the ribs, if you must loosen the ribs as much as the moisture comes out.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to restore the head of the shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, as we have seen in the books; and there are two returns as two blows of the hand.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes. Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails; and it has two holes at each end, as you see, of a palm in length, and two wide at the base; and when you see the marrow open with all the instruments, sit the woman aside, keep your feet still and your legs over, then insert the two nails together into the marrow, and hold the handle of the instrument between your thighs; then grasp your hand with all the instruments, as you did with the nails equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marrow, until the patient feels what it wants.

These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when you behold them appear, the work hastens, and the higher your home is for their quantity.

Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is sprained,
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra. Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it be certain therefore that fumigations are helpful in this case: neither of the ancients has proved the efficacy of fumigation with rue and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman is that we keep her at the retention of the flowers and the secondine if it is this:

And it is seen like a dog in heat, and put the head of the sufferer in the nature, and the limbs large over the fire; and let the fumigations rise over the charcoal, and the smoke until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	No child is born who does not have the solid basis perceived, for it is grasped by an subtle spark: if you wish to cure that which pierces this spark at its root, do not prick with any sharp object, and keep the dressing so that it does not touch; then put on a bandage of fine linen dipped in wine and oil, and then cure with oil until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres. Never comes this stumblement from the support of a wound or an incision; if you cover that support: if it be cured, as we have said of the lead weight.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation</start_of_turn>
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the destruction of the foundation are nodulations, and those that come from the breaking of the foundation are protrusions, or in the space of two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, if it is behind, and includes moisture and white pus or a subtle swelling, and never are these fistulas harmless; and they are known by the patient when he makes an evacuation, or by a sudden movement towards.</start_of_turn
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and half the thigh; and reach as far as the hip joint, and as far as the coccyx bone.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	Or thus one knows at the fistula bursting at the root, and not bursting: and it is only that you bite your thumb index or root, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is swelling, if you insert a sponge or a horsehair, as long as you feel the swelling or the hair at your root; and if you do not feel it, and there is no other pain, no vomiting, no diarrhea, as we have said: remove the hair that is causing the pain; do not linger in curing.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or the urinary tract, if in a jump the urine spurts out, and cannot be held back by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived up to the hip joint, if there is a vein swelling up to the limb; if there is no swelling and the pain persists, if it has already been reduced, and there is no other pain, medicine or support is of no use; and in these bursting fistulas there is no cure except work, and folly of the fools who interfere.</start_of_turn>
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that one which is neither new nor old, hope of health by fire exists, as I have learned; and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he holds his legs up to his thighs, and inclines his thighs towards his belly; then make an attempt to pull, or plunge if there is discomfort, until you see or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root of the limb, if you must bite your thumb index finger, if you feel that the attempt has been perceived; or uncover or feel between your thumb and index finger the flesh or bone, then pull out what is foreign; if it does not yield, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One cannot well heal any wound, but this is often the case; and the help which one makes is this, if one should burn the cautery cautiously according to the size of the fistula, as it is said; and pour toutes les plaies du corps, tant qu’il vienne delez le fondement; and make this two or three times, until you see that these hairs which are similar to a quill of an oyster, must be burnt; and then treat with soft compresses and oil, until that hair has gone, then treat the wound by stitching the edges together and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is still sane, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is still sane, that is good; for if he attempts to do otherwise, and does not pierce straight through to the very foundation, and between his thumb and the attempt there is a thick covering of hair or chaff, and you see the fistula at the point where the covering is broken; if you seize the start of the fistula, and hold it fast before the attempt, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the attempt; then the attempt will be delivered, and the pain will cease. Then remove the hairs which appear like a feather of oil, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it does not please you, and if you are in doubt between the two things, if the fire cautery or the medicine is strong.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two things are assembled: namely, the burning of these hairs and the coagulation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of soft swellings with ointment applied with a brush or chopped chaff, until the liquid escapes, and is forced out by the burnt hair; then cure the wound of the surrounding parts with rough chaff, and these are the dry medicines
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes right up to the bone, and is pushed out by the flesh, if the bone or the foundation is loosened, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel a pulling, and between two fingers is the thumb or the index or the wrist, or if it is near to piercing, if there be naught but flight and hope, by the administration of one of these three remedies: either thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou bind it firmly, or if thou puttest if with force and cure it as first; and do not go too hastily, that thou cover not that which holds the foundation, and bring about the evacuation in the right direction; then cure it as we have said; by chance if it be healed, or thou eschew that covering and the mucus then that it is bound from the foundation; or by pulling or by other pointed instrument; then bind up that wound which is in the wound, as thou dost; and study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the lower part of the foundation: if it be a less grievous thing for the patient.
