Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistula made in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost beside the root of the skin underneath, if you take an attempt pierced at the head according to this fashion:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	...and you must hold the attempt at the root all the way through the fistula until it is at the shoulder.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistula made in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost beside the root of the skin underneath, if you take an attempt pierced at the head according to this fashion: if it is pierced at the root of the foundation, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, as you bite your head or foundation; and draw out the head of the thread, and reunite the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it one or two; and do not restrain at any time, until the thread has overcome these bones that are between two, and are swollen; then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not break through, if you force it to break in every way you can, it will not be too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to force it with stitches if it is deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is sound.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny spa detalle of the fistula is thick and blunt on one side and smooth on the other side, for it is not to be grasped with that which must not be grasped, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrhages are of two kinds: either they are deep in the foundation like grains of resin, small or large, and are cured with pressure alone; or if there is one or more and they are driven out of the foundation and up to the head of the foundation; but those that are driven out again have some moisture in them and are cured with pressure or with a little orange juice or blood, and have the color of flesh; and the cure for those that are deep in the foundation is that you command the patient to stretch and walk about until the foundation is forced out, and the thread is seen; if you are in a hurry, and you cannot hold it with your nails or thumb, then grasp it at its roots; if it cannot be held by its moisture, if you take it to the drapeil or cotton or a piece of chamlet, and strain it out, then grasp it and powder the surrounding area with hot powders instead of cautery; or you can cauterize it as it is said or according to the instructions of the treatise, because the cure of other cures is when it is healed; and if the foundation cannot be forced out, if you bite the patient with a biting and rasping clisteer to force out what is in or under the foundation, if it can be forced out openly; when the patient cannot endure it, and the thread is forced out of the foundation, if the cure is simple, then grasp it with your thumb or nails and pull it out, and cure it as said above, until it is healed, and that it avoids a new incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is suspected that the shoulder has slipped according to this method: take I thread of thread, pierce it with a needle, then draw the thread down and pierce the needle through the other side, and twist II threads of thread from the spool around the needle, and if it is thick; restrain the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and draw out the needle, and do the same with the rest, and leave I to correct the excess of blood; then put upon the foundation I bandage soaked in oil of roses or cerote, and put upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it blanches, and when it is white, if the cure of oil and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	if itching of skin or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There is often itching of the intestines due to worms or constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is suspected that a sprain or fracture is at a point of the nail or the nail-bed, which does not allow it to moisten; then cure it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it cannot be healed, if you must repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until the wound bursts, and be scraped out; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	indeed.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance that appears before the body, and goes out through the pores; and never does it freeze, and is felt just like death from fever, and comes throughout the body, and more so in the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for this is that you take a sponge of goose feathers, or a sponge of strong vulture, and put that sponge on the fever, until the circles of the fever turn the palm of the hand; then move your hand all the way up to the fever, and put it out through the pores, and scrape the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, if you do this with a wasp's claw or iron according to this shape, and be subtle and attentive below:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see it, if you do this with a wasp's claw or iron according to this shape, and be subtle and attentive below: do not perceive it, for it must hold tight, and press it. And if you see it, if you cauterize the edge, if it is before or next to the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a blister.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a blister of silver or gold, or of wasps' honey or beeswax; and never make of these small and great things, according to these things which are brought before them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who accompany me in the treatment of children who are feeble and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	They appear in clusters in small and large sizes, or the belly is tied in such a manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is bound, if you see it, and the shoulder is dislocated either frontally or backwards; and if there is one puncture on one side and two on the other; or if the belly or one of the thighs is filled with medicines from a bladder or parchment, or if it is pierced all around with fine needles, and there is one inch of space between each puncture, then insert in these punctures one strong thread of thread of flax twisted into an X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a nail; and when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument in front of a strong thread, then clip it; and that is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; smear the chief with ointment of oil or balm of egg, or something similar; then bind it loosely. Then hold the hands together of the operator until the veins are full; then draw out the ointment, and leave the patient’s legs exposed, and if the operator sees that it is sufficient, if the swelling has subsided; and if he sleeps all night, this will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you order him to lie down for the relief of a stomach ailment, and the physician hastens to leave, if he resumes his ailment as soon as he is well again.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is swelling of the limb or the foundation or an abscess, if the ointment is as subtle as for a young child; this is the form of subtle ointment that should be placed so that the skin is not strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in this chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on what causes them, and depending on the place or the wound itself, and how it is made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are by biting of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or sickle, or similar things; or that are made according to the laws of bones, as for wounds that bite on the cheek, or on the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, or similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for a wound of the head, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come to mind in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a wound of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the depth of the wound: if you do so quickly, you will make the patient worse even if blood comes from the wound itself; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the affected part; and heed the patient’s swelling of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not recover, if he has lost his appetite, and does not drink wine, does not eat flesh; take out the wound, if there is any suspicion of infection, cover the wound with soft cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no suspicion of infection, put a dressing on the wound while it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by wind, dust, or anything else; I will tell you later about this. If the blood has moved, put on some ointment until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a nail and the edges do not reunite by tension, if you reunite them by stitching, as I will say later about wounds of the belly, of stitching.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and is open, and only held by a single ligament, if the bone is grasped; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as testicles and barley, just like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find or see decay of flesh, and it is not at the bone, if you grasp the limb firmly, and pull it out completely, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched by medicine, if that is the case, and if you find it dislocated, if you can join it with a thread; and if that does not help, burn it.</start_of_turn>
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a minor cure: then put on this powder which adheres as soon as it is moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them finely, and apply to the wound, and bind firmly, until it is well healed and reunited with all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for one does not plaster up medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we perform this treatment alone, when we have neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if you do not put on this powder; but put on some unguents digested, or poultices of ground barley made with water and honey, until it boils over; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone breaks with the wound, and it is small, if you grasp the edges carefully; I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the neck or the artery is cut.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, if there is no other cause except to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; and do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of the blood is with the brain, which is the most sensitive limb; but if the medicine is applied, as for example with chammock bathed in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and urine bathed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this method, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the edges are raw and bleeding, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wound is deep and the flesh is swollen and full of blood, if the artery is severed, and blood flows profusely; if the vein is cut, and marrow and bone marrow are mixed together; if the tonsil is cut, or the epiglottis, and the tongue is grasped, by which the meat will go; if the thumb is fractured above the wrist, do not touch the throat but return it to its natural position; then stretch it out gradually and leave it for a while; then treat the wound with oil until it is healed; if there is a piece of bone in the wound, if the fragments are numerous, do not remove any of them; leave them until the wound is healed and aligned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the cure is as I have said in the chapter.</start_of_turn
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of a lance or a knife</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if thou seest that the wound is open to the wind, know that the wound is mortal; and if it be not deep, and it be fresh throughout its extent, if thou dost not put medicine on it at the first hour, do not bind it up with the skin only, but raise it up from the body, and comfort the patient; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice round; and if thou dost not have an astringent, put in the wound some cotton to absorb the moisture, and cause the patient to sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there be no spasm, do not move the body excessively, neither stretching nor straining. When thou seest the bones in their place, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tension of the tent and other cures, as long as it is sane; and if it cannot be cured, and if there is an opening, drain the pus that has formed; if the cure is to be made as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision with a needle or knife, and it is simple or deep at the front, or if the cure of what is before; if it is great, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is fixed in the bone, and if it is fractured, if you can remove the splinter; and if it cannot be removed, if you leave it to fester, if it aligns the extractions; and for other wounds, as for other members, it is the judge’s decision as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	it is the judgement of other wounds as with us.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The belly is large and painful; from a great wound never does the intestine come out, or the nerves of the intestines, by which the intestines are introduced; the costure is more painful, and never is it better than a small wound than a great one, because it makes the intestines swell more, if they are not returned bit by bit; for when they are returned too much, they cause more pain, and for this reason it is better to leave the intestines in their place rather than to pull them out again. The intestines are returned from the belly in three ways: the two common costures are in the costure of the belly, and the costures of the other wounds are in the ribs and two others are common to other wounds; and all of them are more common with the costure of the belly.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is affected, and there is pain, two things must be done: either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area slightly: moisten a sponge or place a wet drape over it only, or rub with vinegar and salt, and elevate the intestine until the swelling subsides; and do not make this movement restrictive, and be silent that you avoid further swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the swelling going away, if the intestine is filled with liquid or is cooked and callous, because by this means the entrance to the thing is aligned; and if it cannot enter, if you make a hole in the wound with the instrument to remove the clot; the first cure is to be silent that the size is not increased, that you should not cut excessively without necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut from within the curve and do not deflect, and once you have done this, shape it like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestine is pushed forward, if you stop bleeding in accordance with its natural form in its own place, you are mistaken, for this is of no use.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and is at the lower part of the belly, if you order the patient to sit up behind his back and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is at the lower part of the belly, put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and in the same way if the swelling of the belly is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand over that part which is higher than the other; and thus you must order what I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, put what appears between your hands, and join the edges; this is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or more according to the size of the wound, then leave a space equal to the thickness of two fingers at the top of the wound, and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is from the inside of the skin, until you have pierced through that part, and join the two ends of the needle together with three or four stitches; then strain with a double thread around the needle from two parts, and join the two holes of the wound together, and then leave a space equal to the thickness of two fingers, and pierce another needle; and tie the knot of the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this until the wound is completely restrained; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles close up all the flesh, and the thick needles do not penetrate well: therefore it is better that they be neither too fine nor too thick; and do not push the needles too far into the flesh and leather, for they do not close up and open the wound before the suture; and then close the holes of the needles, that they do not bleed the patient while sleeping, and put on patches or bandages over the holes of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them on until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, for there is only one or two stitches to make, and join the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the needle together with a needle or with a strong piece of thread in the middle. And when you have pierced these holes all together, if you remember the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that we usually cut the threads; and leave a space between each suture equal to the thickness of a thumb; this stitch is useful for a wound that has been caused by a knife or something similar, which was more than a palm of the hand wide, and was full of intestines that were two palms of the hand wide, and was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will restore the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound has healed for fifteen days; then the cure will be finished, and he will be healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the madman thought he was dying, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with medicine, for I was in Italy where there was no medicine, no drugs; and I used only oil on the wound twice a day, and applied honey until he was healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will say two ways to stitch: take the needle and pass it through from the underside until it reaches the nail on the right; when it has perceived the nail on the right, if you have pricked the skin or if you have pulled the needle, and you have passed through again from the underside until you reach the nail; and you will understand this stitching if you stitch like a leatherworker, and that you leave once the nail of one side, and you take hold of the other, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does properly, if it is so as none other, which unites the two parts naturally, and joins one chief to the other chief, in this manner: pierce with a needle or chief of a needle close to the other, and make the one pierce only, and leave the two chiefs of the face; then draw out the needle, and make it pierce from the back until it reaches this far side, having two chiefs of the face; then make it pierce one and the other from the back until it reaches this far side, in two other chiefs of the needle that are on the other side; and this is the perfect method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens does not often testify to this, and no one bears witness to it; we must sew up the belly with two needles, or there is thread in the yarn; and one needle must be pushed from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and when the belly has been rotated too much, if the stitching is more tight than in other wounds of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the cost, then put on the healing powder; if it has moved, do not put on any dressing except what is present until the wound contracts; and close the wound, and be bound by the stitches and the edges; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, if you put on nothing, it will start to swell and fester, and move two or three times until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You do not need any other medicine in many situations where wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will not heal properly at its principal parts, you must know that you can moisten coarse linen cloth in warm oil of tempor or rose oil, and put it around the wound, and soak the buttocks; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and this happens many times, if you give them wine vinegar enemas, and the same if putrefaction comes up to the intestines; and pierce it through, and drain what is inside, as when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called 'jeuns' cannot heal when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and because of the slightness of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the flesh leaps from the wound, if it is reset backwards as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is yellowed and becomes black, if you must tie the black part, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the tendons, and suspend the two ends from the part below the wound until the flesh has healed, to align the extraction when the flesh leaps out, and the wound will bow.
de la routure dou boueil	because of the wound's swelling.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in small pieces, because I have seen that one bone has been swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach and became filled and became a fistula, and in this there was discharge and wind; I treated it according to this, and I did not cease to soften it until it was healed, and the wound closed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has no harm in his belly; and there is no point of harm, but it remains in many better conditions, food and drink; and they say that whenever there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligated in a timely manner: take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have grasped the mouth, if you put two fingers on the wound, if it stretches its mouth upwards; then pull out the tooth, and this is kept if it does not slip, and put another tweezers after in that manner until the wound is completely closed; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief tears in the intestine, and there is no further nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast, in a timely manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is loosened, and then tie to the head of this thread one thread of linen that is twisted, then pass the thread through the needle, and in sewing up the intestine, and keep it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce but according to the way of engagement and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, even if it is in one of the large intestines, if there is no danger or discomfort, except for slightness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds that break open or are incisions, when they burst, if called out universally are 'fistula', and even when they are plugged and rent bowe.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the truth a nodation that is hard and white, or one from which no pain is felt; and it is just as plugged as the quill of a bird; neither in clear liquid does it break, nor in thick liquid; neither does it break at all, nor does it break too much; I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no corruption, is healed only by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or the hardness of the flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hardness within, and on the bones, that does not allow the blood to grow; or because there is too much liquid; or because the blood vessels are corrupted, and the matter is of poor quality; or because the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion, and late in recovery, and flees by nature; or because there is a vein or bone: and I have already mentioned all these causes, and their signs, and their cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you should know that I will tell you about the cure for fistula, which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that occur in all limbs due to corruption; for there are fistulas that arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the spleen, or intestine, or bladder, or in some of the bones, or at the spinous process of the backbone, or at any joint of the hand or foot; and if one part comes to the property of the main limb, and the rest remain.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is only toil and ignorance; and if there is no fistula that does not reach the root except as I have said, you must take for granted the possibility of cure, and you must see it confirmed; and if the fistula is straight, if the mark of the burn lies on the bone; and if the fistula is crooked, if the surrounding tissue is tented to sink, for the swelling swells inward towards the curvature; and if the fistula has burst through the skin and you do not know how to cover it properly, if the cavity fills with pus from one burst to the other, for the moisture is too thick from one burst to the other and makes it soft; then as soon as the pus has drained from your hand, that you may know whether there is any bone or nerve, and if there is bruising around the joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or vein, or in any of the things that I have mentioned, if the cavity follows what I have said, and if the bone is fractured, the corrupt matter that is within must be broken up; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded from the outset, if you can cover it up as well as you can, then put in poultices soaked in vinegar, and keep them until the medicine has eaten away the superfluous matter that is remaining; and then put on oily dressings to cover the wound, until it is healed. And if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as I have said, and if the bone is fractured by the fistula, if you can cover it up.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the veins or arteries are not congested, or the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if the limb remains as long as the corruption is entire, then cure the thing cautiously as long as it is sane; and if it is not sane, and it returns as before, take out the nails until you reach the marrow; if you discover and desire as much as you can until you reach the bottom, and remove the whole corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is then sane, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, take out the nails too deeply, for you will not be able to do anything; if there is no other remedy except to leave it to its natural course; and if there is only a small bone that is corrupted, and you wish to treat it, if the extraction is done with a suitable instrument and there is no other bone, do not leave even a splinter; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear, seize and moisten and burn, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not wish to remove them at an opportune hour, put upon the wound something that will prevent putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rigid around the bones; then it will become less painful. And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, leave only as much corruption as is necessary to expose the marrow, then restore the wound; and if there is much corruption, come down to the bone; if you cover it up and leave it exposed, it will become worse. And if there is great corruption, come down to the marrow; cover all until the corruption is gone, and then cure it until it is healed; I will tell you of a fistula that happened to me in my leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There once was a young man of about thirty years of age who had a pain in his leg due to something within the bone, until the matter came out of the leg; there was no cause for him to open it. But he became mad with fear of reopening the wound, and corroded much matter, and a fistula formed, and there came out much pus that filled the wound and moisture from the bone; and he remained there for two years without any physician, until I saw him again. I saw his leg and the medicines he was given, and what cured him of the perforations was great pain in the bone; the bone of the young man became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound a thread in one of these holes, and then circled all the holes, and found that one followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I thereupon bound it in one of the holes and found a piece of bone; it was corrupt and putrid, and the corruption extended to the marrow; I removed what appeared to be corrupt bone, and I believed that there was no further corruption except for that which I had seen; and since I had begun to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, I could not suture it.  I repeated the process, and again found corruption in the bone, which I again removed; and finally I restored the limb, but I could not suture it until I had removed a palm of the bone, and the marrow thereupon leaked out completely.  I restored it again with medicines and it healed well without further swelling or recurrence, except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear the pain, and for fear of death which I had averted.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is blood evacuated thus, but the patient remained entirely well, and there grew in his place a hard scale of bone, which was in good condition and caused neither discomfort nor any disagreement with anything, neither to the ailment nor to any other.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	If the bone is broken in no place of bone, if you must bandage it in this manner: take I thread and stretch it at the head of the bone that breaks, and command no one to extend it upwards; and put I another thread of cloth more coarse than the first, and bind it above the scale which is detached from the bone, and extend the head, if you tear out the corrupt scale at the bottom, and uncover the scale above the place where you see the bandage; and put I cushion or a plug of lead below the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and bandage as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bandage once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part, uncover the entire bone. Then place a sponge soaked in oil on it, and gradually bring the corruption from one end to the other; and when the corruption reaches the end of the bone as we have said, if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint and remove the bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other angle than that of covering. And if the corruption is in the wrist or the elbow, if it is strong in that thing, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appeared to you. And mitigate it in all the ways you can, but do not make the vein or nerve suffer. And take note of the incision and the sutures that cover these bones, for many are the causes of fractures according to the condition of the bones and the appearance of swelling, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their toughness. And for this reason it is necessary to appear similar to the work of this instrument. And note that the work will show you the instrument that you must use, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the methods of diseases; if you doubt the instrument that you must use according to that which is known.
dou feu	If you think the instrument is capable of it, according to what it is intended for
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder doth suffer either by swelling, or by pressure, or by violence; and when thou hast treated that corruption by the means of medicine, it profiteth thee not, if thou dost not cover that limb until the corruption ceaseth; for if the patient escapeth by this means of death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the limb; and the sign of that is when the limb becometh black, as if it were burnt by fire, and afterwards there cometh a blackening of the limb, and it consumeth all the flesh; if thou art hasty in covering, and it be by the percussion of some venomous creatures, as for example a sea scorpion and a viper and the like, if the corruption be at the root of the bone, and the limb be stiff, and thou dost not give it space to come forth until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the wrist, if the callous is at the joint, if the corrosion does not reach the forearm; and if it comes up to the forearm, if the callous is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and nothing but the quantity of its power is of any use; and all the more so when the corrosion comes or goes away: if it comes at the first joint, if the callous follows the other joint; and if it comes or goes away, if the callous grasps all the way; and if it reaches the leg, if the callous is at the knee; and if it comes under the knee, if there is nothing else that can save the patient but to leave the limb broken, and to bind the limb from below and above, and to stretch the skin between the two bones for one span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then grasp or draw out the callous, and put some soft material over the drape, so that the callous does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient further damage and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb violently, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete. Then bind the limb securely with a strong ligature and treat it until it is healed. And I will tell you of a case in which I saw: there was a blackness that seemed to burn the bone, and that corrosion began in the middle of the bone, until it consumed the whole bone. When we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the bone, it healed. But when we took away the ligature, the corrosion returned to its original place. We had to cut off the limb above the lesion, and we did not stop the corrosion. We had to cut off the limb, and we had no hope of saving the matter. We also feared that if we left it, the limb would die, because its strength was feeble. And he recovered and returned to his home, and when he came back he covered his limb, and it healed. And I have never heard of such a case except for this one.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes an abscess in the flesh, and lingers for such a long time that it makes a great swelling of the bowe; then it breaks and bursts, and in the leap of the bowe, it breaks the skin, as if it were a vessel; and the leather that is under is just as thin as a flag, and does not reach the bone, neither the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain", and is not called "fistule"; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone and bursts, it is called "fistule"; and the leather is that if you cut through that leather all around, and even when it is thin, as if it were a flag, and does not yield to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect that the skin has hardened, and the corruption is not in the marrow, and the skin is thick as parchment, if the surgeon of clists is present: look if the tumor is large and the bowe is foul-smelling, then make a clistery of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take barley, oil, and alum, equally, and mix them together, and put the skin in a vessel on the fire, until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey; then take of this according to your need, and make it hot and thick, and instill it into the tumor, and press the wound; and leave the medicine on for two hours, then take it out, expressing it out; do this several times, until the tumor is softened, and the bone is healed; and never make a clistery with vinegar, when this medicine is not present, but take vinegar of figs, and let it drain out, and then make the clistery, until you are certain that the tumor is well healed; and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar, if the clistery is made with vinegar and honey or if there is a little bit of alum dissolved; or make the clistery of honey and wine, because honey has the property of softening and washing out, and the wine makes the wound breathe; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the tumor is well softened, if the clistery of this makes new blood in it, and you take pounded chamomile, and make a poultice with oil rose and wine; or make the clistery of other medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken of their properties or treating of unguents; and if the wound is small, and the pain of the clistery does not reach it, if the swelling is done with a nail, put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or balsam, as much as it is swollen; and if the wound is too wide, if the edge and it leave so much skin or the clistery can enter, and if the discharge of the wound is below, if the head or more of the wound is below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the shoulder is out of joint, if you leave the limb dangling without support, it will not return to its place; if you do not cover the limb adequately as you see, it will appear in such a manner that the shoulder will be pulled below its lowest point. For when the shoulder is out of joint, if you leave the limb dangling without support and do not cover the limb adequately as you see, it will appear in such a way: that the shoulder will slip forward slightly and leave nothing of the limb; and take solidifying medicines to bring back the blood, and place over a cloth that covers all the blood; then close the forces from the place where the opening was made to the widest part of the limb; and keep the shoulder aligned with the other cloth as much as possible, according to the amount of the opening. Leave the greater cloth only for a moment after the shoulder has been reduced; and whoever comes out of the opening often helps to reduce the shoulder, and the patient often feels a sensation of relief, whether it is poison or a wound, or enough, or digested, or undigested. Take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has progressed to such a degree that you see the nature of the leap on the limb, if the blood has already clotted, and approach the health. Then take off the bandage in the morning or afternoon, and when you take off the bandage, if you see the other cloth, renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it sustains a violent pain that does not subside after a while, its bones split and do not rejoin.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes out after a long tension, if you do not quickly arouse from sickness, for sickness is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes out after a long tension, if you do not quickly arouse from sickness, for sickness is approaching. For there are some who delay their poison in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if it comes late to the breast, and is prolonged, it is because there is too much moisture in substance and little in virtue, as with the diaphnet of vinegar, because there is a great deal of vitriol in it, which is the last medicine. Take diaphnet and mix it with rose oil and the juice of five wines in substance; then confect and use it. This will make the wound swell up, when diaphnet is not present, or take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them up, and sprinkle them on honey when the fire is out; then smear it on the wound and extend it out of the breast; and never give an aristologist anything long, and celestial roots, which is as much like flour sometimes and coriander; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them up, make powder of them, and sprinkle them on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it. And if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this remedy, then its poison has penetrated deep into the bone, or caused stiffness of the limbs, or swelling; if the cure of fistula is like what we have said before.
