de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the incision of the abscess.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that originates from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the heel, or by chance arises in other parts; and when it is inflamed, and care is not taken, if it comes to be an abscess of the thumb, it contracts and swells as much as it contracts the root of the thumb, and by chance it contracts all the way; and there comes corrosion up to the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the bone is large, and the color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have treated it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, if you must, you must do everything that is superfluous that remains of the thumb, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help when the bone is sound, and the thumb is healthy; and when the thumb presses on the sinew, and it begins to swell, and becomes black, if you must put in place all the soft parts of the thumb except for the bone, and put on the cuticle again, and carefully and gently remove the soft tissue, and put on some medicinal ointment and corrosive substances to burn away everything; then treat the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the bone is corroded and the swelling is great, do not hesitate but cut through; for as much as the corrupted bone is concerned, it cannot be healed. If you see the bone cracking, if it is in front as it is said, then cure it until it is healed. If it is inflamed and swollen, and there is great pain, it is best to remove it first; then cut through the upper part of the bone, and keep the cut from reaching the cartilage which is under the bone, for the patient would feel too much pain. If this happens, put something on which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be taken away.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two thumbs which arise from the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some part where there is bone, and never is there a nail, and none are born in the root of the joint, or are born from our thumbs directly.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in no way of doubt does not move; he who is born at the joint of the arm by chance moves; the size of that which is fleshy is slight, in part like this: size like the root of a large sponge.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grieved to cure: if you hold him under cover.

He who is born or must at the rear of any doubt, if you must, first join the rounded flesh around the bone, then join the bone to the corresponding degree to that, then cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from birth, or from wound, or from burn, or from other things.</start_of_turn>

des vils	Des vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Hair is black, thick and full of black fluid, which comes in greater numbers from those who work and walk and bear burdens, than from others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give her any purgatives, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment for fire is in two ways: one is with the forceps, and treat the black blood; the other method is to cauterize the vein and then drain it entirely
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first raise the affected limb hot and strong until the bone is not felt to bend; then strain the limb of the patient from below the hip joint up to the part just below the knee; then cut the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size; then sew up and drain the black blood from your hand, from the tip to the heel, until as much blood as the patient can tolerate has drained away; and then close the wound and command the patient to eat flesh in moderation; and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The ailments of the limb are as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there is hair, then put or bathe it in warm water, and elevate the limb until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, if the fire burns, then cauterize the end of the vein, or in the part below the ankle; then cover the skin with lint, and draw the vein from the heel up as far as it breaks; and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out or the skin seems as if a white thread; then remove the clot from below, until it is freed from the skin, and then apply a slight pressure, and cauterize once more; then draw the skin up until it breaks, and leave it in place as you did before; and do the same again, or several times if necessary; then leave it, and cauterize at the end; and draw it out until it is entirely freed, then cauterize; and if you do not draw it out and lift it, if there is a strong double hair at the root, grasp it and draw it out, and there will be blood loss; keep your hand steady on one side and the other, until it is finished; and keep still, because if you move it, you will not be able to draw it out or lift it, and there will be harm to the patient; and when you have finished, take out the foreign matter from the wound with coarse wool and vinegar.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the eye is contracted and tortures and surrounded together, and it is not straight, as we have said, if you must force it open, do not cover it; and treat it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of fire from which we cover the eye if it is crooked, do not cut through, but only cover the vein; for if it were slight, it would cut the vein, but let it be large as we have said, and this is the form.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is contained in the arm, in hot places or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises from another place except the arm, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decay of the leather, as it comes from the inside of the serpent's body and towards, is contained between leather and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there is a sign of the commencement of this vein if there comes into the limb a very great inflammation, then it is chained to the bone and the vein begins to swell like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the limb is open, if you think that you should wrap around a piece of sponge from one and a half inches to two and a half inches, and the nail, and leave the sponge in the limb, and every time that there is a point of pain, if you wrap around the sponge the nail and the nailhead; and if it is too long, if you cut off a part and wrap around the remainder, and do not cover the root, until it is all out; for if you cover it, it returns to the bone and causes swelling and pus or death, and is harmful; therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and without delay, and that nothing remains or is broken; for I have seen many times that this vein, when treated with five fingers of sponge or ten, and one hand has already come out of ten fingers, and when you cover it, if there is one hair or perforation, and you pierce to the end, so that all is out; and be it emptied of the matter which is inside, and bring to the limb medicinal poultices that do not cause pus, and cure as with apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow joint, or on the elbow, and immediately there comes blood from the rupture; cure it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow joint, or on the elbow, and immediately there comes blood from the rupture; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "bull's disease", because it often causes swelling in the calves, and is a small vein that arises between skin and bone, and runs throughout the body ascending and descending, and is felt well throughout the limbs, as long as the skin is taut or is pulled, and sometimes spurts out; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, worms and blisters or abscesses. And there is doubt of its malice, for when it runs through the body and reaches the head, and comes out again, it often breaks the oil (fat).
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot force it out, if you can, then bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, and hold above and press down with your hand, and if it does not come out, if you cauterize the fire on it, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is when it comes near the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, tighten the bandage around it, and hold above and press down. And you must make use of the patient of medications that dissolve harmful humors, and feed him nourishing foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot force it out, if you can, then bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, and hold above and press down with your hand, and if it does not come out, if you cauterize the fire on it, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is when it comes near the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, tighten the bandage around it, and hold above and press down. This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs, and it spreads from limb to limb; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to see a sick woman, and found her with her arms swollen, and saw a small swelling in her armpit; and after that, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, more swollen than anything, as much as half an egg when it breaks from its shell; the pain departed from that shoulder and settled in the armpit, and then after a while corrected throughout the limb, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it often happened that it returned to its place.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed to hear how it twisted back and forth within the limb, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I believe that if one tries to move the limb without pain, it will not move; but I do not believe that, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because her bones were dry and her veins were exposed, and because of that appeared that stiffness; and I do not understand according to this reason those who are delicious, and who have moist bones and veins filled up

When you see the cure for this ailment and the patient feels the pain, if she opens her eyes as we have said, and if the lower and upper eyelids are swollen, then take hold of the eyelid as tightly as that constraint allows; and cauterize the eye. des saiettes	When you see the cure for this ailment and the patient feels the pain, if she opens her eyes as we have said, and if the lower and upper eyelids are swollen, then take hold of the eyelid as tightly as that constraint allows; and cauterize the eye. Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The bandages are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they cause.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of these things is such that there are some with large points, some with small points, some with hair, and some with bristles; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and that which bites in no limb bites in two ways: either in the main limb, as with the brain, shoulder, liver, stomach, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it bites, it signifies death, I will tell you later. Be aware: if you delay the extraction of this arrow, for there will follow numerous complications; and when this is the case, I do not tell you that the arrow is not deeply embedded, for if so, cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the arrow bites and pierces the bone, and blood spurts from the vein above the brain, and there is scooping, swelling, nausea, vomiting, and stiffness of the tongue, and spasms and mixture of senses, and black vomit; and sometimes without cause of nosebleeds or deafness; and sometimes the speech and voice are lost; and a white moist discharge like pus appears, and also blood-stained urine; and if this sign tells you, do not delay, and remove the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the fracture when it breaks or cracks is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were fastened to a hard thing, not without pain; and by chance the fracture moves like a poultice, and in dark blood, and comes with chills and cold sweat, and fainting: the patient is in doubt that he will survive.

Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled out an arrow from the chest, which was hanging or belly-down, and I thought it was dead; and when I had not seen it move for XXX days, if it did not move of its own accord; I cut at the arrow and pulled it out, and there was no mishap.</start_of_turn>
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if I see a wound in the chest with an arrow stuck or back, and the wound is deep; I take out the arrow from the wound, and I do not bind its natural inclinations, and I do not find discomfort in any of its natural works.</start_of_turn
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And thus it happened to another man, that he was pierced in the face with an arrow, and the wound was closed; yet he continued to suffer great pain; and many others had the same experience.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And thus it happened to another man, that the king’s son was struck in the eye by an arrow, which was deeply embedded in the flesh; and there was a great decline in his face; and the arrow was completely extracted three days later.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is much injured
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would try everything possible to stop it, and I did not feel it; and there was no pain or tingling in his left ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I put on an absorbent dressing and a digestive plaster, so that it would not swell; and the arrow came out by itself
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put my thumbs on the wound, and held the wound steady, and kept the patient’s hand long tense, until he felt the arrow inside his body; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the corrosive medicine on the wound by hand, until it was overdone, and held it, and felt the head of the arrow which was coming out of its place; then I closed the wound by means of that medicine, as long as the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and it went well for three months, and then grew so large that I had to remove the nails, and I held it from one side and the other, and I could not stir it; therefore I continued to torment and irritate in various ways, until I finally took away the nails, as it is said at the end of this chapter, until I had finished, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nevertheless, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or you have spoken of the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on that which I do not say, for the books do not teach me everything; but you know the masters well enough to know well enough about great matters, and about what is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, descending from the things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not issue from limbs or that they are ficxed by force only because of two methods: either by the left hand or by the right hand, or by some other way; and that which leaps forth by the left hand or by the right hand, is an arrow that has penetrated the flesh, and leaps no more ever.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, if you leave it until the chariot is carried in, and rejoice in the issue; and if it is fixed in the bone and cannot be moved, if you leave it alone for a few days, and move it little by little; then it will jump. And if it does not jump, if you pierce through all the entrails, until the belly is swollen, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the bellies of the brain, and some of the signs that I have said to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days, for if the splinter comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the splinter is not firmly grasped only by the bone alone, and does not advance beyond the surface, and remains in the patient for several days without mishap, if the pain persists.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is firmly fixed and cannot be moved, if you administer tarterises round about, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is firmly grasped only by the bone, and it cannot be seen, if it has every effort; and if you feel it, if there is no palpable instrument that can cover it; and if you do not take hold of the wound by force, and by the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the pain is great as the wound is large; then draw out the splinter if you can, and if there is an ear attached to it that it holds, if the cartilage which is fixed from two parts to the muscle that you take hold of, then break or crush the ears of the splinter as much as you can, until you can draw it out; and do so cautiously that you do not break the splinter, that you draw it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not manage it once, if the limb remains entangled, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If blood flow is disrupted by the discharge of blood, which opposes the treatment in this chapter; then beware of incisions of the nerve or vein, and take care as you would to remove the arrow without causing further damage; or break off the fragment or leave it firmly in place; and put the patient in the position in which he was when the arrow went in, for this is the greatest aid that can be given, and if you cannot do this, follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The wound which comes from elsewhere, or if there is no visible opening, or if the skin is swollen in that place if it is seen or suspected: then raise up the limb until the teeth can take hold, and then remove it immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it does not come out, if you leave it in, and then attempt to extract it again until it comes out; if there is blood in the wound, if the blood vessel has been severed; if there is marrow in the bone and you see it, if you must administer a hook, if the hook has passed through the point of the arrow, then draw the arrow through the hook as well, so that the point of the arrow is at the level of the hook; and then draw out the arrow, and if the arrow is hooked, if the hook is at the point of the arrow, in order to ease the extraction
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the dressing is surrounded, if you must, seize all the surrounding flesh or the venom is there, if so, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the bandage tears or breaks, or on the belly or at the bladder or the ribs, and it is close, and if you must cover it, cover over it; and hold the wound and the nerves still, and then extract the foreign body, and then suture the wound, if necessary; and cure as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the nails with which we treat the saiettes is similar to the beak of an owl, and thus is this form:</start_of_turn>
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, small, and medium, according to the amount of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the shoulder is like that of a bird’s wing, in order to push out the point of the dislocation, as in this manner.</start_of_turn
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tweezers to push and to grasp if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common colour
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins which we must take into consideration in this case, namely: two veins that are behind the ears, which are above the eyebrows; and two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the armpits, which are above the nipples; and a vein that is in the forehead; and a vein that is at the base of the nose; and two tendons that are in the collarbone; and two veins that are in the upper arms, which are called the brachial veins; and these are the veins that are above the elbow; and two veins that are below the tongue.</start_of_turn
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that we commonly speak of are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the costus, and is called the large vein; the middle one is called the fast, and is composed of the cephalic and brachial, and is called the large vein; and the brachial is either on the right or left side of the costus, and is called the small vein, and is above the scapula, which is the one from which we speak, which appears openly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar is the vein which is between the radial and the ring, and if there are two veins; and in the leg and the foot there are three veins: one is below the prominence of the left costus, and the second is the popliteal which is at the ankle of the right costus; and the vein which is called the great saphenous, which is in the ankle of the left costus; and in the other leg there are three veins like these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to expel the old blood; and the quality of the blood, as I have told you, is that you raise the patient’s head and rub the hand or the veins are rough; then you tighten the patient’s neck with a pin, as long as the two veins behind the ears depend from the head: that is if the patient has a throbbing pain in his head or feels his pulse throbbing in his head, it is a sign of infection; then take the lancet and pierce the vein up to the bone, then keep your hand over the whole of the vein above, and hold and pierce the skin and the vein well together, and make the blood spurt out until you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries which are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, soda, and mustard, and has the color of tears of rain; and the quality of the physician is as I have said: and that the patient strains his neck, as the two veins open wide; and he feels a tingling sensation in his thumb, then he signs the incision; then he takes hold of the thumb above the index finger, and pulls out the lancet, and pulls the vein above, and the clot, as he has done in the two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his necessity; then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on cotton; and then the swelling subsides, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this and its treatment and extraction, or its beginning from the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is as valuable as that from the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face, in embolism, and in redness; and the quality is such that if the patient turns his head violently, the vein bursts open. Then take the instrument which is called the "fosseur," which is thus formed:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is as valuable as that from the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face, in embolism, and in redness; and the quality is such that if the patient turns his head violently, the vein bursts open. Then take the instrument which is called the "fosseur," which is thus formed: put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then pull out the patient’s head, and ligate the vein until it is whole and never again open with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable for me to say that the flame should be too strong; and the same with the other side, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are two palms wide helps with swelling, tension, redness, and oily discharge, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is such that if the patient turns his head violently, as before, the same will happen; then do the same, and either let the blood clot, for a long time with a wide flame, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make an incision of the blood, as much as you are able, and then ligate the vein, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein does not flow if it is cold, and in excess, and in disease of the face, as with migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient is hoarse, then strain his neck to your left hand, take the flame and hold it long, and insert it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily, and do not start until now to correct; and do not go too quickly, and make the correction according to your need, and then bind it for one night, for it is moist and restored. This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps to loosen swelling, and to commence mixing, and with moist of diseases, and with swelling, and with corruptions, and with herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient grasps his collar with both hands, as we have said; then the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient sits on one seat, then open the vein widely, and draw blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then close the other part in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and gently tighten the veins moderately, so that the patient is not stifled; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the herbs.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms and shoulders helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and toothaches and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Of the blood of the herbs, if it is to be made to flow from the patient before you, hold his head down as I have said; then open the vein, and observe two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left side, and know them by their darkness, and by that which enters them has small dark veins: close therefore one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, if you close the greater one from the front, and do the same with the two smaller ones beneath and above, for this is a like manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the blood beneath the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins beneath the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and holds the tongue, and looks under each rib towards the costal margin of a black vein: close therefore one and the other, and do not press too hard, for there are arteries there
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which are commonly wounded are usually sound in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp flame, or by means of an olive-shaped incision as with cut nails, and is called ‘anesil’; and they are large and olive-shaped according to the size and breadth of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the cautery is known to be mild, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is another method for opening large veins filled with visible blood, which contain much blood and blood clots; and this is the form of the olive-shaped flame incision
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier the small veins, or there is small yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to cause ailments such as swelling of the throat, and the jaw, and the tongue, and the belly; and it is necessary for the health that it should flow smoothly, and that it should avoid the artery which is swollen
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he grasps the heel and blood flows, if he must hold it back as I have said; and must not be moved by the flame, but cut off like an anesik.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the pulse does not clearly appear, if you must remove it, and bind another in its place; or do you wish no blood to flow, or do you leave the vein open in the arm: it will appear clearly; and grasp the flame as an anesik, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the blood vessel going black, if you must therefore remove the limb, touch the vessel until you see the pulse; then mark the place, then bind the limb, and grasp the vein with the flame; and take care not to cut the artery when you see the limb swell, for that is the artery: withdraw from it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurting high like the urine of a child, and it is pale and frothy, know that it is without an artery: hasten then, put your hand over the wound, and hold your hand steady until it stops bleeding; many times it has happened to me. If the bleeding does not cease, bind the arm tightly and leave it still, and do not move the patient; and be wary, do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not stained, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts open, for the head of the shoulder retracts; and close it off without delay.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bandage and wring it out, and take half of it and lay it well over the wound; if it stops bleeding, that is good; if not, if the physician says so, powders that stop bleeding; the bleeding will not be great in many situations because of the small size of the wound, and the ability of the limb to move.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle aids in healing by closing the wound from above and from below, for it is composed of the basilar and cephalic nerves, as we have said; and it is necessary for the patient to bite on the nerve which is below, and if he does not bite too deeply and finds the nerve, it swells and the wound is either healed or becomes worse; and this nerve is often split many times, and if it does not split in some people due to its delicacy, it is necessary to take the blood from an anesthetic instrument and withdraw the nerve from your mouth.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is of long duration.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein aids in healing, by pulling the wound shut from above and helping to close it; and it is necessary to bite on the olive or mirtin flame to stop bleeding, for this is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Whatever, it is better to ask for help the first time, and do not grieve if it fails; we can always begin again. And by chance it will burst in someone's face, as it cannot be the first time, but it does not grieve anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must not be drawn for no other purpose than to maintain health and repel diseases; and let the blood be taken from one of the three veins that are or should be: namely, the cephalic, facial, or basilar. And it must be taken at the beginning of prayer, during fasting and after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be drawn at the first or third hour, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood that is administered for diseases has no fixed dose, but that whenever there is need for blood or nourishment, in all hours and at all times; and it must not be drawn from children under twelve years of age, nor from women for more than four months up to puberty
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither shall they treat those who have passed 60 years
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone feels well, in whatever way, if it is known that he has retained a bellyful of wind, if the veins do not draw out the harmful humors from the intestines by their roots; neither too much meat, nor too little, neither too fat nor too lean; and if he has eaten with violence, vomiting, and swelling of the belly, and multiple attacks of sickness, and work, and sleep, and fasting; and all these things together, or by some weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not too large, by meat, drink, and medicine, if you can; then give him a bath or wash, so that nothing hinders the healing, and keep him warm until the third part of the night, as we have said; and keep him busy with work, worry, and luxury, and similar things; and bind and join, and make the patient sit higher than he was before, and gently stroke his arm two or three times, then remove the dressing from the middle; for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot be corrected without; then stroke the wound with your hands, until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the patient with the flame of a little oil, then put his left hand on the wound and hold his hand for a moment or two until he feels well, that the wound does not swell and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings to the physician, and if some of them are filled with wind, that when one places the flame on them, they recoil from the flame and will not open; and this is what happens in this case. And if the vein is opened, the wound is too wide, for in this case the physician must be advised of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein severs the first time, that is good; if not, one must repeat the process again until the bleeding stops.</start_of_turn
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed, and the patient hopes for relief, if he leaves it for a year or two, without immobilizing the limb: by chance will come abscesses spontaneously; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; and if the bleeding is slight, or without a visible cause, and you doubt that there is as much blood as you see, if you are confident in that bleeding itself, without any other flame; and do the work quickly, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often occurs when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If thou seest the limb inflamed, if thou delay not the bleeding, put upon a little piece of lint of oil, for it doth soften the body of blood; and it doth remain in this limb the lint which doth hold the oil; and give the oil-soaked lint in the wound so that thou doth stop the course of blood; and this doth cause a tingling and swelling about the limb when it is put upon the limb. If thou withdraw it too soon and it is too thick, it will burst.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess which has happened many times, even though it is not dangerous unless at this time or the opening of the vein is small, if thou art in a hurry, put upon the limb a wet sponge and a little cloth, and hold it for an hour; and cover that you have done after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after some days no black or green mark, if thou seest not; and if thou seest, put upon nothing of aloes or myrrh mixed with vinegar of calamus, mustards, or anything similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of blood in the armpit: put your hand on and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave then out of all that we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but make it [the wound] i.e. emplastre dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it to darken as long as it is red; and if you see it large, leave it to dry until it is subtle; and if it is too thick, let it cool down.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be known to him who is plain and strong, and has need of the extraction of blood, that we make the wound larger, and let the flame be large; and to him who is weak, do the contrary, and make it healthier more often, and must do so by cutting across, not by pricking; for this way of bleeding is saved from the decay of blood and nerves, and is worth more than bleeding for a long time is wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him who needs to be given food with the blood, it is to be given soft bread in the juice of pomegranates; if he is pale, if take blood three times or four. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before the blood soft bread in mustard sauce, or in honey syrup with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he pricks at the blood, after the issue of moisture of blood, then it is appropriate that he swallow coarse barley and aromatic oil, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees his arm swollen, and recovers again another time, if it is known, when it is soaked in great blood, that it must recover and recover, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has severe pain, if he waits until the third hour after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who has seen himself cured of another kind, if he must wait until the second or third day?
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which is already swollen, and causes fever; if one can drive out a great quantity, and expand the opening until it cries out with bones; then that when you have treated all the conditions of the blood, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not come out in place of bones, and this happens many times, when the patient is negligent; and it is not right that you should see it slip from the arm, and cause the blood to go out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press further; if it is crooked, that you extend the arm greatly, because that would be bad; but leave it until it goes out a second time; or you touch at the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein is forced out with the blood, and put on some oil and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not constrain it, as long as the incision is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood the second time, if the same vein is the same, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is stained in place for that which is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And thus concerning the bleeding, if the patient grasps his hand in warm water, while the blood clot is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound will open well; then pull it out quickly, not too wide nor too long; or make a large hole and place the finger close to the wrist joint, and if that does not suffice, grasp the hand in warm water once more, and leave the clot in the water until you have enough; and if this is the case, do not reinsert the hand in warm water, for more is put into it than in the case; and the blood of this vein is more precious than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the saliva of the right hand is valuable for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and immerse it in warm water, until the vein is emptied; if it comes out whole, and if you pull it through and if you grasp it throughout, do not grieve; and do not grasp too tightly, for the nerves are already loosened from their sheaths, and then grasp the hand once more in warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not attempt to remove it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will stick and prevent healing, and do nothing.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do the same as I have told you about the other side.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the spleen is worth for all diseases that are caused by an excess of heat in the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the reins, and tumors of the legs and arms, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient has too much pain in hot water, and rubs on the belly until it boils, and lies down on the joint of the bone; if the belly is at the ankle, and from there the bone comes out with the blood; such a thing is either a great wound or a large wound, or at the ankle, that much blood is worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you keep guard of the nerves which are sore, and keep the limb straight as when you are grasping; and let the flame cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient must be bled the first time, if he does it again the second time, because his blood is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the spleen of the other limb equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The thigh bone is at the ankle of the buttock, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that flows abundantly.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient is lying or bathing, and the wound has been strained two or three times at the ankle, for otherwise it will not open; and if it opens, no matter how you try, and even by cutting through; it is better to leave it alone, for the pus is thick, and it will soon fill up again with its own hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find any blood flowing from the wound when it opens or if there is little pain, and towards the little toe, and you take care of the wound as much as you like, and even by cutting through; it is better to leave it alone, for the blood is thick, and it will soon fill up again by itself.
des sainies de ventouse	bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selon ces manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sang, ou sans ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	There are two methods of bloodletting: one is with great heat, the other with moderate heat.
