Bloodletting that is done by cutting and by extraction of blood is best done in twelve pulses, of which one is at the top of the head and the other at the nape of the neck; two on the two costal cartilages of the neck; two on the two armpits; two on the wrists; two on the two arms; two on the two thighs; two on the two calves; and bloodletting does not treat any disease that comes from an excess of blood, until all the diseased blood has been evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is necessary to vomit, or by custom, if the physician commands it at the beginning or at the end, or during the course of the illness; for there are some who, when they must vomit, have a great weight of chief; and there are some who find swelling and redness in their face, in their head, and at the collar, and dark circles under the eyes; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and vomited blood; and there are some who dream of it and see black spots and blood and death.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when moisture has come to the middle of the month, we command the patient to keep the wound covered for two hours more.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps with the pain of the head … which comes from the dark circles under the eyes; and it must not be given before the evacuation of all the humours; for this vomiting is in lieu of the blood of the cephalic vein, and must not be given to those who are of a hot complexion or who have a cold sweat, because this causes great discomfort; and for this reason it must not be given to those who have cold fevers.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who remains silent in such a state, if he becomes oblivious, it is necessary to place the ventouse somewhat lower down due to the doubt of obliviousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind blowing in the neck is in lieu of the blood of the head and the bile, and because of this it is worth a great swelling of the face, a splitting of the windpipe, and all sorts of things; and it is necessary to bite fiercely, for if it stays too tightly, it will cause obstruction of the throat or the stomach or the liver.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The swelling of the neck is worth as much as the pains of the head, vomiting, diarrhea, strangulation, and toothache; and it is in lieu of the blood of the bile; and it is necessary that you order the patient to express his hand to put it on, that he does not cut an artery, and does not vomit blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds blow cold from the coast, and causes chills of the head, and pain in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in lieu of the ailments of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds blow cold from the coast, and causes chills of the head, and pain that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swelling of the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and order the patient not to be too tightly bound, for the flesh is soft, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the flank is as much as blood vessels under the foundation, and there are diseases of these, and it is advisable that the swelling be large and coarse, that it has mixed well; and by chance, if it were slight, if it should break, it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The hair of the legs becomes loose and wide open, because it attracts blood from all over the body, and causes an ancient pain of rains, and of marshes, and of the bladder, and makes swell the flowers; and is in lieu of two sophies and two calves, and all of them cause the body to swell afterwards for a long time, and bring about vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is that you apply it immediately when it is empty, and do so steadily, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing so until you see the blood flowing freely and swelling; then withdraw, and reapply the suction cup, and take care of the position of the body, for there are some who have too much hair, and pores that bleed: if you cut once only, you will cause great wounds and deep veins; and do so cautiously.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, if you must cut twice: the first time to remove the large blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If he does not moan excessively, if you may wound him for the third time; when our wounds trail blood so profusely, so profusely that our hands are stained a third time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins burst with blood, if we see them swell often; if they are not quickly treated, if they are inflamed and swollen, and if they are perceived to be perforated, it is useful for those who have thick skin and tough veins, and who have numerous pores, to apply an aperitif and dissolvent oil of the following: violet oil, sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; or in the springtime, cresson oil, or radish oil, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the swelling is large and cold, if you take bitter oil, or balsamite, or rue oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If he has strong nails and large pores, it is not appropriate to put oil on them, but it is appropriate to wash them afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or of elderberry, and of thyme, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have superfluous humours must rise from wine strong, or from aquavit, or from decoction of rue or chamomile, or from other such things; and must not cover themselves with a bandage before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and must not sleep after the ventosation, and must get up when they are to get up and when they are getting up.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are pale from eating too much and being inflamed; if they must take cold things, as pomegranate seeds and radishes and lettuce easily, and other such things; and eat barley gruel, and broth of wheat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if they take honey syrup, and fragrant wine middle between strong and new, and eat barley gruel, and eat barley meal and eggs and almonds; and when they have a cold, they must drink more than eat; and must give to others no meat triacle or muscate before or after the ventosation, in order to comfort the main parts; and be discreet about it, but it must not be that they do not drink it
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made with a knife are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and podagra, and upon the belly and the bowel and the flanks and the heel, for these members do not suffer much from wounds upon their surface, and one does them only to draw blood from a limb into another, as we do when we place them upon the nipples when they do not bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as we do when we place a blister upon the belly and the bowel to make the limb limp; and to relieve the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, for it relieves by its attractive force the swelling or frees the stone from its place; and thus it becomes elevated when it is placed upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained congestion. These blisters are administered empty without any dressing, and never together with fire or water that is cold, as in the case of pleurisy; and in such a manner we fill the blister with warm water or with water when there are herbs that are covariant with this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the compress administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two large and half palms of barley and either the cost or the price of an inch and a quarter, as for driving out an awl; or it may be of flaxseed, before if it does not harm the patient in setting it on the limb; and there is in the middle of it a twig of flaxseed or iron, to hold the bandage in place, and these are to be of a size appropriate for the disease and the nature of those who take it; for the blisters of the intestines are not like other things, and the leanness is not like fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And must be put on the limb: grasp the bandage with the thumb or index finger, and place it through the twig which is already in the ventouse, so that it bites either at the back of the ventouse that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and two must be placed either on the wound or as we have said, so that when we pull, if it goes up, we remove the ventouse; and grasp the lining as before, and repeat often, if you are in doubt.</start_of_turn>
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse therefore which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all severity, there is no verge or perforation, and it is only administered when it is plain of severity, and is placed upon the limb as little as possible; and this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	No needles are administered except in limbs where it is impossible to put on venuses for their small size, such as bones and teeth, and similar things; and in their skin devoid of hair, such as the groin or navel, and other similar things; and the quality of the patient is such that when you find needles that are in soft, smooth hair without causing perforation, if you take them out; and put one in a sweet liquid, until they are limp, and they have nothing in their belly; and then either drain the vein and the needle, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the needles; and when they are full and painful, if it is possible to put on the needle, put it on, for this is worth more.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this does not suffice, if you lift the limb easily, then gradually with water, mix well, and then press; if the limb still swells too much afterwards with the skin of the wound, if you pour water over ice, put on, as long as the wound is extended; and if the wound is multiplied, put on broiled vitriol, or scraps, and similar things, until it is extended; or you take out half of the black bones, and leave them until they burn out in the limb, if you stop now; and if you still have more to do, take on other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take hold, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you put in a needle until the wound is closed, and then put on, as long as it feels the blood, if it stops bleeding; and when you see that it bleeds again, if you sprinkle on a little aloes and bruised saffron, or charcoal, if it will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear me, dear son, for the book tells us nothing of this chapter, neither in ancient books nor in letters; and for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found any good example of it. I know of nothing, save from the ancient books or from what I have learned through study and experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made it clear what instruments are necessary, as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book that it contains words and chapters which put understanding into the science, and teaches the truth, so that those who are proved in this science learn and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain occurs, if you must hasten the healing of the patient on one side and on the other, if nothing else hinders you, if weakness of the limb, or youth or old age, or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and if the patient is suffering from cold bile, that is to say, cold humors, and oily and sour substances, and does not drink wine, does not eat greasy foods, and does not fill the veins with too much meat, until you are certain of the absence of any post-traumatic inflammation or expansion of the substance in the limb; if the patient then resumes their former activity, it will be for the better.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, if you command that the patient be nourished with meats that cause great swelling, or if he has viscosity, as with millet dough in water, and wheat germ, and testicles, and spleen, and pancreas, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at this part of nourishment, the muscles relax and become more brittle.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Know that bones broken in various places and decrepit do not mend well by themselves according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs; neither do those that are too tender, as bones of small children. But there is no remedy, except to support the broken bone with great tension which has arisen, and to join the limb together, so that it becomes firm as before; and do not move it from that point. For this reason it is commanded to nourish the body with large quantities of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the marrow, and others by cutting, as with the size of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And with regard to the fracture of a bone, it has its sign and its proper instrument in its restoration; as one remembers from its place. The fracture of the bone is known by that which causes it to twist, and it opens well by drawing, and by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting or fissure or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move your hand, but put on medicines that will come afterwards, and then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And wounds that break that go into the marrow, and are two parts of the joint, it is now necessary to put them in order equally, as well as after the incision; and if the incision is hot, if you leave any marrow, as long as the incision is not calmed; then put it in order with the muscle that you can conveniently and safely lift, and the wounds that restore the limb are lighter than the restoration of those who have pieces; then strain, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they are two parts, if it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or a string and your hand; and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb that break are loosened, if you rejoin all the fragments in their place on the muscle that you can conveniently lift, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient any lesion or pain; and adjust well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the dressing is good and is not too tight, do not press as they do who make come by their work to cause swelling and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is fixed in place, if the patient keeps it still, neither awake nor asleep, neither turning nor moving in any way; and keep the limb well secured so that it does not cause him any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at its proper place, it must be put back into position so that he feels no pain; and keep it straight so that there is no twisting when restoring it; and the quality of the limb will be as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limbs are various in small and large size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as bones and joints and the like: if you can cover them with soft and fine cloth; and for those that are large, such as thighs and arms: cover them with a wide and strong bandage, because the large bandages embrace all the great limb and constrain it equally, so that there is no slack; then put on firm supports, three turns or four according to the limb, and constrain the hand a little more than the rest, then go up to the break and constrain it less, than the break itself then lets go of a little of the break; and soften the limb a little more, as much as you take hold of a large part of the limb, then take back one bandage, and re-tie the support above the break; then put back at the bottom of the break, and constrain it moderately, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said at the beginning of this chapter; then put in between the supports some bandage or cloth, so that they are even all around, and then tie everything up with strong bands, and put on your boots well made above, if there is no opening or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is swelling or abscess, put upon something soothing the abscess externally, and which hardens the swelling; and leave it in place for some days. Then strain upon your toes, and let them be half of a broad cane resting firmly, or of wood from which nails are made, or of barley straw, and let them be as this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the staple which one places upon the fracture be greater and broader than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the part of small or great size; then strain upon the toes in the same way as before, and tie a thread around them immediately, as in the first hour of the fracture; the tighter the thread, the less; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen. For if the thread is thick, as some fools do who make their knots of linen thread, and it is great error, because the knot will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will not hold properly.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is numbed by the bites of the nails after stripping in the groin, if you put sponges of lint or coarse cloth on them, they will not bleed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bone fractured, and the bone is broken, I shall speak of the cure afterwards.</start_of_turn
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And those threads which he cannot bear to withdraw from these stars shall break all the bones of the first hour.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not permissible to put these stars in place except after five days or seven, or more as you deem necessary for the safety of the afterbirth; and once this is done, the manner of the ancient plasters will restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundance of eggs, and make this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common manner of plastering that restores the fracture in many situations, as well as for women and young children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of packing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and flaxseed and linseed and saffron and arabic gum and mugwort, in the amount of ten; myrrh and aloes, in the amount of five; chamomile, in the amount of seven and eight. Mix them together and grind them into a powder; mix this with abundant eggs. If the patient’s complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is good for torsion: take mugwort and chamomile, each in the amount of X; myrrh and aloes, each in the amount of VIIII; acacia in the amount of VI; chamomile in the amount of X; mix them well, and confit with water or abundance of eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones that have loosened from their sockets, and relieve the pain that arises, and reduce the swelling: take new linen, and moisten with oil and hold on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These methods do not permanently restore the joint, but they are good for relieving post-traumatic swelling and pain, and for repositioning bones properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of displacement that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pell leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods include restoring the fracture of the bone and diminishing the remaining swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violets, barley flour, and rue; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, soak with vinegar or water, and apply
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess hardens during restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of vismalve, seed of flax, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, of all an equal part; and bruise, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for certain things that make wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two, not too soft or too hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have us put something dry and warm upon the broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and other such things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions or fennel seeds, and beeswax, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone is not moved from its place; if you do not loosen by hand from the start, and if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, stop and loosen, and support the limb now; and put on a lighter bandage, and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, and lift the limb until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, wet with water or rose oil, and bind up with a nut, until you are sure the abscess has drained; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure the pain is gone, then repeat the binding loosely, and a little displacement, do not strain too much, and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that at the incision point there are swelling, redness, pain, and swelling, then you must immediately stop and bind it firmly, as you did at the beginning.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not happen to the limb anything of what we have said, if one must force it loose, do not do so before three days or four, or five or seven; and in no case leave it for twenty days, as one sees, until the swelling has gone down and the limb is nearly back in its place; then the restraint must be more severe than before, and the limb must be well fleshed out, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, the swelling will not come down; then take an aquaphoric solution and bathe the limb every time you loosen it, every third day, and cut a little of the sinew; by this means the swelling will be reduced in the limb and the patient will recover quickly from what the fools have done, and will restore the limb correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various forms of breakage</start_of_turn
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many are the ways of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures which are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is fractured throughout to the syphus which is broken off from the bone, as is made by a break or crush; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or if the spear pierces the bone in a reverse direction, this is called a «complete fracture»; and the wound of these fractures can be large or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	and if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the joint, or any other similar thing.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a fracture that approaches the joint that is below the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and whether the wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound which is closed in the bone as subtly as a nail, and the fracture is slight, and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by a wound from a stone, or by a thorn, or by anything similar, and causes the piece of bone below to enter the cavity, and the limb is bent as when people sit upon hot pots when they are placed on the embers; if between the bone ends.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this often happens with those who have soft bones or joints like children; and in all these ways, when small pieces break away from them, like stars; and I will speak of this in more detail later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these ways of fracture from the separation above them, from tension, and from the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary mark is known by this, that when one has discovered the bone, and has rubbed fat on it, if the fracture is black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no other mishap, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, feverishness, and other similar things, if these do not heal, doubtlessly there is a serious underlying condition.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you see no imminent danger and hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you arrive in this state first, and it is in the armpit, then you must immediately remove the bone in front of the wrist toward the thumb
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you delay in removing the bone in front of the elbow toward the thumb, the tissue surrounding the bone will become corrupted, and there will be the accident that we have mentioned
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a break of the bone comes right up to the skin covering the brain, if you must open the fractured part: if you grasp the patient’s head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the figure of the wound more roughly than you can; and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or incision, if it is aided by this, and that you fill the cavity with moist cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the incisions are calmed, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then as you twist the bone to heal, this is done in two ways: one way if you grasp the tail of the fracture in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have various sizes of nails, some wide and others narrow, and be blunt or pointed, and of iron indeed; and over a light burden, that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through it, even though you administer nails with washers, do not pierce too deeply beyond the test of the bone; and must have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if the nails come out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have washers for all tests; and this is the form of the two manners of washers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put one washer on the bone, and turn your two thumbs until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the washer back in another place a little after, and do everything around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more skillfully than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have moved the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have if you have nails, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated, if it is possible, rejoin the fractured part which is loosened from the bone to all other instruments resembling a chisel, but make it more tense and subtle than the other chisel; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not neglect any scale, if the bone is slightly fractured by some instrument; then close the wound with stitches and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the liquid is very strong, and that is its word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by displacement of the muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and hold the pointed end of this incisor lens, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not split the bone in two, but let the fractured part rest against two costs; if the incision is towards the bone, then hold in place with a small mallet so as to press the bone gently inwards, and take care of the dressing that is below; if it is too close to the bone, if the bone is slightly fractured, for it is better to leave it whole in its place, rather than to damage it further.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing the skin, cut the bone as little as possible from above; there are small pieces. If you can, return the toughness and remove the scales of the whetstone that you must have in various quantities, to bring about in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you see before great raisers, and afterwards more subtle, and do not cease to do so until it is well.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle fractures, it is convenient to bring about the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is discovered, it is commanded that you take a drapeil of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in oil roset, and put it on the wound; then take another drapeil doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and oil roset, and put it on the first drapeil; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not harm the wound further; then administer from above another linen, and do not bind it more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines as follows: radix of iris, flour of times, powder of incense, and ariste, and similar things; mix these things together and put them on the wound, and administer again the appropriate medicines in moderation; and keep the wound clean, that you do not leave it bloody, neither do you leave it gathered up, for when it is gathered up on the head of the brain, if it is crooked and stiff, it brings great harm to the patient; for when anything biting is put on the wound, if it does not desist from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	And keep that the wound is perfectly closed, that you do not open it further, nor leave it open, for when it is closed on the brain, if it is crooked and stays, it causes great harm to the patient; for when one puts on the face something biting, if it is not driven down by its base.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If black bile does not come forth violently except by the medicine we have placed upon it, that some virtue has, if you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drape, and put it upon the affected area; then you shall cure it in the manner of cures that it ought to be cured, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then follow the manner of treatment that is suitable, as long as he is sane.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if you must drink your little toe or pierce with needle that does not please you, and put equal pressure on that fracture within your index finger and on the heel, until it returns to its natural position; do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the arm, and it cannot come down naturally, you should know that you must put a strong splint on the forearm at the level of the elbow.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the fracture is of two parts, if you must do it again, and hurry to restore the first part if you wish; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, bathe the head of the toe where you attempted to bandage, if the fracture is in a part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must bind up the limb another way, if the break is there; and make the bandage so strong that it fills the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer shall move the tents in the burrow, and die each for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not seem to understand. And never should one put goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is much snow drape it round, and keep the brim steady, and blow the patient among them; or do as you will.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if there comes snow after the procedure while you are working, if you put some butter or cloth soaked in oil rose or some vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez. de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no break of the skin, the fracture is often incomplete, not completely broken through, except for the fragments within, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the lower part, to bite down with the index finger of the opposite hand in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take hold of the index finger of the right hand, and grasp the fracture lightly, and move it apart with the other hand by force, and hold it equal
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., it is necessary to administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes swelling, or if a tooth is strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken mandible cerote on and put on a pair of double drapes; and put on a large bandage well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and bind it on the tooth as you wish, and command the patient to rest, and eat lean meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the limb is deformed, if the bone is fractured at the third part, and then reset it in its place; put on a plaster cast with fine powder of beeswax with plenty of egg yolks or flour of alum, after you have broken the cerote; and put on a clean bandage, and if the plaster casts have dried, and the limb does not move, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it is healed in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if there is swelling in the apostemes, if we have already said many times.

Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if the edge has burned according to your necessity.

And when you have boned all these pieces, and there is no more movement, if the wound is wide, put on some covering over the wound, in order to prevent infection, as long as it is necessary.
de la forcele	because of its force.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forced fracture occurs often before, behind the shoulder, and if it is broken and loosened in two pieces, there are fragments, and it is the lightest to restore; or if there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the fracture is with a wound, if you have two assistants, let one hold the limb that feels the forced fracture; and the other extend the head towards the part; then put the fracture back in place, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of wax, or linen, and be large as you need; and extend and hold the forced fracture, and strain the ball at your hand, so that you can put the fracture back in place as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to support the head of the humerus in its proper position, because it comes out of place, you must know that the patient lies supine on his back, and put the arm under the armpit, namely the middle armpit, and keep the minister there until the head of the humerus is raised up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find fragments, if you must, make an incision there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot reunite by any means, if the head has become fractured at one of the incisors that you have made; but that you put under the armpit the instrument which is called the forcele, to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not crooked, and should be as wide as it seems convenient, according to the size of the bone and the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bone; and when you are assured of the apposition of the caulking, if the wound is large, or if you doubt the apposition of the caulking, if you employ the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the aftercare comes, if there is moisture, let oil rose, ale, and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensitive to wounds and to the touch, is that you put on the bone powdered rosin and egg-white, and put on thick stockings, and put a sponge under the armpit if you need to; then take a very broad bandage of a palm width, and put on two layers of cloth over the stockings, and the rosin; then take a needle of three nails wide and long, and wrap around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is fixed; and put the needle on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the collar, and under the armpit; and leave the shoulder resting, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture steadily, and that you see clearly that the needle does not move from the fractured bone, if the fracture is slight, or if you doubt the setting of the caulking, if you employ the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and keep it still until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to anyone.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is fractured or displaced from its normal position, it must not be forced out but must be gently released by touch. If the limb appears according to the fracture, and is reduced according to its natural shape, in every way possible; then pour the fracture with fine powder of mill with abundant eggs, and press firmly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle splint, one wider than the scapula, and keep the splint firmly in place so that it does not move from its position. Watch carefully the limb’s every movement. Every time it becomes loose, if the splint is released, put the limb back in its place and keep the patient lying down; and the scapula will be restored in approximately twenty days or less. And when this number is reached, if the limb is free, and so be it, for it is not a bone that has become loose readily.

If a piece of bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it is on top, and the bone, do as we have said in the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess above.
de la brisure dou pis	If a piece of bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it is on top, and the bone, do as we have said in the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess above.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is never broken in the middle, but it often breaks at the start. But it often breaks in fleeing.
