Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and slightly force them equal in every way that you can, until the limb is as it should be; then put on dressings and stamp with the thumb a little salt or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind tightly to the bone, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round behind, and strain gently, and reward chest every hour the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you see that it will not hold, because of corrosion or purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, do not delay, but loosen and remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the way of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and slightly force them equal in every way that you can, until the limb is as it should be; then put on dressings and stamp with the thumb a little salt or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind tightly to the bone, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round behind, and strain gently, and reward chest every hour the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you see that it will not hold, because of corrosion or purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, do not delay, but loosen and remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the way of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fractures of the ribs only come from great blows to the back and the head, and they do not swell except for these things which are slippery; and one can well know at the inquiry how they are.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is if you put the break back in its place, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a support, and hold it with a bandage, if you have need of it
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is downward, if the patient feels great pain, and swelling, as with pleuracy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and there is swelling, and vomiting, and great loss of blood, which is a serious matter, and the former has put on great pain.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it is necessary to administer nourishing foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to break the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for those who are unconscious or dying.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there is life in them, let them be conscious.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one should put on stockings over the limb, because of swelling; for this is similar to reason; however, there is doubt that the stocking will hold back the excess fluid from the limb due to weakness.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, and put on tents between the ribs to make the girth even, then either cure the pleurisis, meat and medicine.</start_of_turn
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the belly, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is necessary to cut above the fractured bone, and if it is necessary to place the dressing, then you must break the bone slightly, and drain the wound gently, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with supports, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If a wound bleeds profusely, put upon wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and lay upon the limb; and cure until the bleeding stops by itself on the edge of the wound, without adding anything else, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points the rib, and there is doubt to the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in dressings, namely instruments to hold the face; then it must be cut through the bone, and treated gently, and then the two layers of the wound must be sutured, if it is large, and it must be cured with sponges, until it is healed. And if pus comes from the wound, if you put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the wound; and treat while the bone is being held in place, and if necessary above the rib, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a fracture of the rib bone, and often it rains; and also at the shoulder blade.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	When this happens to anyone, and you know whether it will heal or not, if you see his hands limp and limping and dying, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if there is no sensation in them
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	When it is deadly in multiple situations, and if you move them and feel well when you extract and prick them, the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will recover, if we put treatment on it
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if anything similar comes to the spine at the waist, you must know whether there is blood or not; if there is, take care that the piece is softened, and if there is an accident which is in the hands or on the back, the wind and the evacuation will go upwards; and when it is softened on the belly, the evacuation will go upwards.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When it is softened on the back and he looks to sell, he cannot do it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	The pangs that cause death: if he does not work diligently in his wound
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these things do not occur, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the remedy is that if there is a wound at the base of the hair, put upon the spine oil of rose or oil of nutmeg of an egg, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comfortable and drying plasters, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone is dislocated, if you can cover over the limb; and unite the two ends of the wound, if it is large, with a bandage, then cure with oil that binds hair, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "fracture of the jaw", if it is on your left hand, and put it equal to the right hand at your waist, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you must; then strain, and if there are broken bones, if you leave it like that, and unite the bones, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	and the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if there is no sign of improvement despite prolonged treatment, and if it is rejected by the flesh, it brings pain to the patient, swelling, and causes the fractured part to bulge out.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the fracture is high up, when you extend your hand over the fracture as long as you are over the break; and you mark what is fractured and how it is positioned; and if the fracture is only at the hip, if you make it even, as long as it is in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is low down, or if it slopes outwards, make the patient lie on his belly, until the fracture is restored.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you put on the shoulder, then put on a staff of wood or bone, and hold the arm steady, so that it does not move; and keep the limb still, as long as the limb is even.

And if the swelling comes again, do not touch it, until the swelling has subsided; and put on what we have previously mentioned; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be held, if there is no further mishap; and that is the remedy.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the fracture of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And thus he makes two pulls of the arm, and holds the patient above a seat; then he grasps the broken bone in the wrist with his hand, as if he were making a handle of a bowl, and holds it up without any weight or the assistant extends it downward; then he puts the arm into its place, as well as he can manage, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should support the patient on his chest, and tie his arm to his neck, and order the assistants that one holds what is on the fracture at his hands, and the other to hold below at all the bones, and to extend the thumbs outwards from his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, strain the blood from the wound, from the wound itself, and extend the thumbs of the attendants to their part
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is close to the head of the shoulder, you must know that you must place the thumb of the sufferer over the elbow and the other towards the heel, of the wound; and if the wound is on the heel, you must put the thumb lightly, with force, as long as the wound is equal on the shoulder and the heel; then put the wound equal, as it should be, and strain, if the pieces do not come together by themselves
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the fracture persists, do not strain it for more than thirteen days; put on a clean bandage in oil of roses until the fracture is calmed; then strain and put in place the support for the break; reassemble the arm on the shoulder or chest; put on the dressing and strain the bandage on the arm and shoulder, so that the arm is steady, without anything hindering it, or without moving the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints and put under the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and put between the splints two spaces equal in size; then strain on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the swelling of the limb, and the tightening, as we have said, in the morning when you restore the limb, and you doubt the wound, if you leave it closed until the seventh day, as we have said; then look for three days, that the swelling does not increase or arise in the limb, or that the discoloration does not arise in the limb because of that which is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the swelling persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such things happen, if not after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back and has his hands on his stomach; and put a cushion of wool an inch thick under the limb, and look for an hour or two, that the limb is not moving, or that the ligaments are not softened; if the swelling persists through the power of medicine, and you do the thing which we have set before you, in part as the meat must be at the first warmth; and when it starts to recover, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the limb must be restored within forty days of all; and then one must loosen and administer poultices and ointments to the limb to restore it to its proper position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the fracture is slight and bloody, if it does not move for a month or two, it must be loosened.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure du bras	...of the fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and is like a nail which supports the pouch; the other is large and is like a weight, over the small thumb. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, or sometimes both; and sometimes the bones break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, the restoration is slight and the healing; but when the large bone is fractured, if the healing is poor, it is more painful than when they are fractured whole.</start_of_turn
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the small bone is fractured, if it is recommended to extend it slightly and make it even.</start_of_turn
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And when the large bone is fractured, if the limb must be drawn more strongly; and extend over one cushion, and hold the hand of the arm higher than the other, and the small hand must be lower than the other hand, and let the patient cross his arm over himself, and one cushion in front of him higher than the patient, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or from the elbow to the shoulder, and another limb from the shoulder to the elbow.</start_of_turn
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then he sets the eye equal, according to its better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking [of a limb], if you put something in its place, and if there is none that will prick [it] now, and you cannot leave it there, if you leave it above and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in the breaking of a limb, as I have spoken of in this chapter; if you take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	Then at the beginning of the restoration, if there are afterpains, if they are thick, I apply cerate made of rose oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and I apply it superficially, until the afterpains have subsided.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then I put on the cerate and I put in place the powder of the mill with plenty of egg white, because I put in the nails, and let the nail of the bone be the strongest and a little wider than the others; and there should be six nails or arms in more or less positions: either that the nail is in one of the bones, or in two; and it is strained more on the nail than anywhere else, and it should be washed less often, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the covers that are on the nail be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rest the limb and the tendon afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any other misfortune happens to the limb, if there is swelling that happens to the limb, then you must raise the limb high with warm water, until the swelling has subsided; and leave the limb still until it is relaxed.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the traction, and if the tendons are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, if the situation permits
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot be brought down in the limb, because it is too great, then shalt thou soften it somewhat, and leave it alone for a while, until the swelling subsides, and then stretch it again.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, keep it unbound for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or when the limb is healed, then he must keep his hands on his collar, and his collar even, and be careful not to move or eat, and sleep on his back; and keep the wound covered for thirty days or more, according to the composition and complexion of the patient.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	As at the back of the hand, we often find fractures, and they do not cease but to increase many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is fractured or broken, if it is suspected that the patient is in great pain, let the patient sit still and straight before him equally; then put his hand on the extended towel, and extend the fractured bones, and put them even with the others; and put on the plaster and the bandages, if necessary; and put on a splint according to the extent of the wound; and if necessary, cover with a bandage of linen
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the elbow towards the belly of the limb, if you make a loop of bandage, and command the patient to strain his fractured limb; and then strain with a long bandage, and if necessary, put on a splint as large as the limb, and strain it as much as it is possible.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is lateral, order that you place a splint above and below the joint, so that the thumb is overextended and straight, then bind it all around the thumb, and keep it closed between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture is neither above nor below, if it is a pouch, if it must be equal, as it should; and strain it with the thumb, and if you see that it does not move, if the fracture is elsewhere, as in the index or any other, if it must be equal, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or bind them all together, holding the wrist, or place a splint on it, as with a pouch; and take care in restoring and arranging the burn, and secure what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and it is seen when it bends forward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if either of the ligaments around the knee joint is torn, and the other is ruptured by the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If also it is close to the knee, and then either the ligament from the knee joint or the collateral ligament is torn; then put the hand on the bone equal to two hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then put on the dressing and the bandage, for there comes no pain from there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is swelling around the incision, if you leave it calm and return to your work and cure; the knot is made in a hasty manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a bandage doubled in two or three, and to drain the surplus; then rotate the limb until the talons reach the root of the nail, and pass a thread long between the thigh and the limb from below the knee, and pass the thread over the top; then rotate on the limb and the thigh the bandage, and put on the dressing on the fracture, and put a pin on the bone of the limb; then put eight threads between the limb and the thigh of coarse cloth to bring about the same tension; and as you go up the fracture, and less you strain; then take out two threads that you passed between the limb and the thigh, and put three pins on top, which are below; and cover again to the level of the nail, until you see below the piece; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it be, and there will be no further swelling or pain or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling, if it comes loose, and if the bone is pierced, if it is necessary; and if it cannot be moved, if it is necessary, to cut the thread and draw out the bone; and cure it as we have said, when it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone snapped in this case that one sets it, as in the shoulder and the arm; however, in the restoration that is made, it does not bring any pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And if the bone is set within a day, or less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin region.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that in the groin district has recently burst, but it rains often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it breaks, if it is not just a tear, or a wound, and if there is pain, and feeling of pain, and this is felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus, if it be set right, do thou put them even which are round about their shoulders, so that they be well assembled together; then put the bandage on, and set a round cushion, if thou canst manage it, and strain it as it may be strained, and reward all the conditions that we have said before, as for instance chaut abscess and other like; if thou dost set each mishap that may happen, so that they be sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	And thus, if it be set right, do thou put them even which are round about their shoulders, so that they be well assembled together; then put the bandage on, and set a round cushion, if thou canst manage it, and strain it as it may be strained, and reward all the conditions that we have said before, as for instance chaut abscess and other like; if thou dost set each mishap that may happen, so that they be sound.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hair that in the groin has two bones, of which one is called the “muscle” and the other is called the “fossa”; and there is breaking in all parts as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, if the limb is twisted from every part
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted from front to back
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	If the big bone is broken, if there is great pain, and it is seen well; and it is twisted from its place.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When it is necessary to restore the dislocation, extend the limb fully and make it even, and bind the joints evenly; however, if the fracture is severe, there are many pieces, and the extension is less severe and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have completed your work, if you take two strips of coarse cloth that will embrace the limb from one side to the other, and are as long as the limb from the knee to the toes; then encircle in two places with bandage from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle, and to this binding do not allow the limb to bend either to the right or the left, and thus it is well; and no one should administer anything with a length greater than the limb, and if there are bones, that the extension should be less violent and more gentle; and align according to your ability.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones due to violence.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in the bones of the limb there is no fracture at all, and there must be something else which causes it, for there is doubt only in many cases.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the limb, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put the limb so that it is almost suspended in the air, as if it were flying, and then put the limb back on the ground, where the bones were raised, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put on a little bandage under the bone at about the distance of three fingers, and bind the limb steadily, and cover it with a cloth or other things as you deem necessary.</start_of_turn
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is not better, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there be two breaks, if you restore them as we have said, do two of the hands; then put at the end of each break a pin corresponding to the length of the break, and make a mark further on; then put the thumb that I have mentioned there, and strain immediately; and if there are three or four, break, and put on each break a pin corresponding to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone; and keep it firm on the head of the thumb over the belly of the bone, if you keep it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember that you must not neglect the other things that I have said about other breaks, as we have mentioned; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural bone of the woman is broken, if she sits enlarged, then incline towards the lower back and hold her back; then fill the belly of the woman with wool, and put as much as I stop; then draw out the woman, and keep her back and front, and then pull out the wool, as long as it comes out of the nature, and bring back the bone with the stop; and when she sees the urine, if she has pulled out the wool, and when she has urinated, she will recover, and do this for seven days or until the fracture is restored. If this is done, take a bladder of barley and bind a string to the opening and pour all the bladder into the nature; then blow through the string until the bladder is emptied. The nature will then restore the fracture; then fill with wool and leave it for a while until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or a woman is fractured, if it is reset as we have said concerning the thighbone; these fractures are not hidden from him who places his study and his habit on it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration: enter then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put it in the groin; then wrap it with cloth and leave it for two days or until it is healed.
de brisure avec plaie	From break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with wound, even if it is large, as for example the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or the like, that he be sound now, as the testimonies we have mentioned bear witness.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, if the remaining vitriol is sufficient, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the break once more in the same hour, or at most two hours, if the swelling does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if swelling comes, if you leave the restoration until new night, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch either a third or a fourth, for you will risk coming to a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if a bone breaks beneath the skin is appears uncovered, if it is known that you must place your hands lightly over the wound, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the swelling does not appear to you to be able to place your hands equally on your hands, if the implement which is of iron, which has about .vij. or .viij. of length, and the large size is in accordance with the quantity of the wound; and because of this it is necessary that it should grasp .iii. or .iiij., as much as is necessary in a wound of fracture; and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not pierce the compression on the limb at your work, and let it be before and behind, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palainche", because it is known that the curved bones should be placed over the head of the apparent bone; and the latter must once again be equal to the former
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well hold the bone, if you must copy the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you see that the head of a bone has slipped from its socket, or if it is necessary to pierce or cut, at your peril; then remove that which is loose from the bone, leaving only the rough and tough parts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the limb is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, the swelling that was not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it remains in its place, then I drape it in black vinegar, and properly keep it in this state; and do not put any cerate or other substance on the wound, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars after the limb has been restored, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area as much as necessary, according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has been the cause of madness among fools, and has caused the patient to die or become paralyzed on many occasions; and let the stitches be finer and softer than the other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the cause is not serious, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it is not possible to place it on supports; but cover around with strong cloth, and bind tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days swelling at the wound, if the bone that you placed on all sides has become loose, and there is healing of wounds, as with the application of ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must bind the limb once a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And you must keep the limb immobilized in a moderate degree as when it is gently flexed backwards and forwards
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists, and cannot be healed but returns to its original position, with small pieces of bone displaced, because you must try to close the wound, and remove all these displaced fragments that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is fistula at the limb, or other kind of corruption, if it is possible to cure it, according to what is written in this chapter above
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and is open on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other bones of the great limbs, if it is not treated, for many times death comes from this; but leave it until it has healed; by chance it will mend itself after twenty days or thirty, and then cure the wound if you wish; or if you do not wish, leave it alone
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out from the root.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Hair comes out from the root many times after the heat of the bath, even when it is near the joint; and the thing to be seen is the figure of the limb; and by chance one cannot make the limb do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care that the patient does not bleed: if you administer astringents, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and other things, ensure that you take neither of these things, or all of them together, and mix them with wine that is astringent or with plenty of egg or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain them well, and do not remove them from the hands for days; and then remove the dislocation, and repeat the process until the nodulation is bony; or you tie it to a piece of lead that is well made; for the property of lead is that if it is bony all the swellings under the limb are overcome. And if the nodulation has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above is great, and to make the superabundance apparent; or you leave it without a drain, until it is bony, and cure it when it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb is weak after the dressing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is restored, and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it: either because it was too tightly bound and was not properly loosened; or because there were too many bands, and it could not move freely; or because of many wounds; or because of too great a movement, not in its proper place; or because there is too much blood in the limb, if it is weak
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient move more gently, and to keep the limb firm, until the swelling is gone; and give him baths, and make him drink wine and eat; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice absorbs the great swelling, and the blood flows smoothly, until the swelling returns to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is fractured open, and the limb is deformed, although it retains its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be fractured anew, and many have had this experience in our land; this treatment is blamed, and many evils result from it; and by chance the patient dies. Although, if the swelling and torture are fresh, if you believe they have arisen from warm water, or soft herbs such as rue, ivy, and meadowsweet, and similar things; then make an application of a soothing poultice, like good aquaintance, and take the nourishment of rue, and mix it with grease of gelatine or oil of sesame, and apply the poultice on; or take fat figs, and grind them with bran of colocynth, and similar medicines that mitigate the vomiting.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone fractured by continuous rubbing and length of time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Or else, do not move the limb during its fracture hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, if it covers the bone, make an incision as slight as possible; and place cushions and a study in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes about, if it can now be put back in its place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one waits too long, if the limb swells up, and by chance one should reset it, there will be pain at the root; for this reason one must not move it while it is swollen: many times this has caused swelling and other pains; however, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable again, then leave him alone, until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb gently with oil, and massage it lightly, and cure each limb as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have commanded the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the wrist.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws have become loose and clumsy, and the dislocation of both is as follows: either they are a little too rigid in their place, and soften somewhat; or they are completely loosened, and hang downwards, and cause the tongue to hang out of the mouth, unable to close it, and to swallow.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, if it returns by itself several times
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and accompanied, if you must necessarily reset it, do not grasp it; and in such a manner that the attendants hold the patient’s head firmly, and look towards the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two must be loosened, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them all around
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep his eyes fixed on the mark, until it returns to its place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even though the two mandibles are together, if they arise from hot water and oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is well clotted with soft material, put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with linen; and let the patient rest on his back, with his arms resting between two cushions, so that he does not move either forward or backward, or strain himself, but take moderate nourishment, until the pains are gone, and keep the jawbone firmly closed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not return to their place at a moment, and are not converted at their leisure, fever and sweat will arise, and sometimes vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be used for a long time without causing damage, and is of no use once the pain has increased, and one often feels it.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	If the patient lies perfectly still on his back, extend his arms; then press the limb towards his palm, and it will return. Then put on the support and bind it, and strain it; the limb that is towards the heel cannot be loosened. If this does not happen, and if it is loosened once, if you leave it alone, it will come loose again as we have said; then put on the support and the bandage, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in this way the limb will be brought back to its place when it is freed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hair that grows on the shoulder is not disvalued except in three ways: one is that it is disvalued at the lower part of the shoulder towards the elbow; the second is at the upper part of the arm towards the shoulder; and by chance it is disvalued at the upper part, and this is common; do not disvalue it further at the shoulder, nor at the elbow; and often disvalue it downwards towards the shoulder, even among those who have little hair, for in these jumps it has become necessary; among those who have enough hair, it jumps at points and returns at points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there happens blows or fractures, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with a hot abscess, and care must be taken that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is certain therefore that you must be certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocation is known when the limb moves towards the shoulder and makes a difference between the diseased and healthy shoulder; and you will find between their difference that the shoulder joint has a socket, and the elbow touches the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a fist. And the patient cannot move their hand back to its place, or move in any way; and if it is dislocated high up, if it is not hidden, because you will find it clearly at the touch. And this manner of dislocation is not sufficient to restore it, when it is new, or when the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician takes hold of the painful limb above, then places his thumbs under the shoulder-blade, and holds the joint forcibly upwards; and the physician takes hold of the limb and extends it upwards, because thereby it is put under tension.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said above, if you must know, the patient should be bathed in warm water; and you should administer a soft and soothing medicine, such as a decoction of fennel and melilot in water, or administer it directly; or you should support the patient on his back, and put under the seat a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, then put the patient’s hand on the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant will hold the chief of the patient’s shoulder, so that it does not move forward; the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains according to this method: that you make present a force that is greater than the patient; and that you place two fingers on the shoulder joint, and hold the shoulder up, so that the patient hangs down; and another attendant will treat the hand of the patient backward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak to bear any weight, if he can do nothing with his hand, the dislocation will come back immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And so we must do in another way: if the head of the shoulder is like a stone long in the earth, which is as if the arm were a nail, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then put some ointment on the patient, but let him have a bandage over his hand, and let the patient lie down with his hand long by the side; then extend his hand forward from the other side and the joint will return to its place at once; and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, do this remedy: take two thumbs and three fingers of good size, which has the thumb resting on the base of the little finger, according to this fashion:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the sufferer, draped in a cloth so that he does not see the physician, then put his hands on the patient’s ass; extend your arms on the patient’s back, and place the sufferer on the arm, and his arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on an angle of an elbow of a span, and either extend the hands downwards or leave the wrists hanging outwards: the joint is now recovered.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is recovered, in whatever way that may be, if you put his hands on the patient’s ass again a span of wool even, then put a cushion of powdered rye, with incense and an egg yolk, on the whole shoulder and around, then strain from the ass downwards, and turn the limb over the cushion, and embrace the hand to his collar, and either keep the hands down or let them hang loose.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And must keep him from moving, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move more after five or six days, and the limb will be healed; and if it is stiff and is not softened, it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is forced out of place by moisture, or for any other reason, if you must administer cautery, apply it three times as a front or in the chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and if it does not heal after seventeen days, and the limb still cannot be raised, then know that the nerves at the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the dislocation will never be healed in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is from front to back, and the arms, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the limbs, and if another bandage is administered; and it must be cured as long as it is painless.</start_of_turn>
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing the wound comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later movement, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the wound comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later movement, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing the wound comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later movement, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the painful limb with the sound limb, if the wound appears open to view.</start_of_turn>
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot rest upon the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must keep it immobile even after it has been reset, because if you reset it again, if by chance it had come loose, it would be useless to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back at all, even when it is at the back.  It is better to leave it as it is than to reset it again, for it is more painful and by chance it brings death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is possible to restore it, when it is like this that you can bring it back, extend your hand with both hands; and extend your arms and hands as wide as the pain of the joint allows, from the thumb to the little finger, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and pull from the root of the bone that is dry.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension; then twist the arm from its shoulder, and having enclosed a long and wide bandage; and when you have looked at the joint to the hand, if there is any oil on the joint to soften it, then put on a dry plaster and strain the arm, and leave the arm bound to the painful limb for some time, and then loosen it.</start_of_turn
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.
