And if the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you notice that it does not move smoothly, repeat the displacement and rejoin the limb, and leave it thus for a few days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and massage thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or put on the joint a fatty mutton nail, leave it in for a day and a night, then extract the nail and the pus; and when it has sweated, gently massage the joint, then replace the nail, and then repeat once or twice, until it is healed. If you see that it returns to its place, put on a poultice of moist chaff filled with burr and press on it; if it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than any other joint in the body. It is necessary to restore it to its place immediately, even if it is loosened, and even if there is swelling or a wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put your hand on a table with your palm facing outwards, and extend your fingers, look at the hand so that you can put the palm on the joint, and press until it returns naturally; it is necessary that you watch to see if it is well placed. Then put your hand back on the table, palm downwards, from the extension to the reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and look put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that is well. If not, if the strain of the soft tissues is appeased after the incisions, and you leave it in its place to recover.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you do not wish to put it back after a few days, it will stay dislocated; and do not do anything to the patient except soften the hand, and do not attempt to extract anything. If there is nothing else to extract except by cautery, do that in this case, and by chance there is no other remedy.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you put on the plaster we mentioned before, then strain and leave it for three days, then take it off and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well, and if there is no pain, if the joint is swollen with warm moisture, then massage it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	until the dislocation of the shoulder of the arm is healed.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the hand detached from the forearm, never from the back of the palm or the belly; therefore let the hand remain detached, and support the dislocation at your pouches until it returns, then sustain the head of the hand, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it for two days, and then put it back as before; and do not bind it, as we have said, and loosen the bandage, and move it, and bind it again; do this often, until it is narrow, and do the same if it is detached from the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is detached from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient is in danger.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the blood egestions flow in the opposite direction, do not hold it back, and many times the limb is softened, or the two knees or two arms or one leg; and many times the scapula moves to three parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbosite": it is cured if you can prove that the gilbosite originates from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from impacts or from similar things, they say was formerly cured by great words; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the heel, there is no remedy; and the same with that which comes directly on two coasts, we can cure nothing but that which comes from behind, as I have said; and that the patient’s face should be stretched out one inch equal, and should have strain from the toes; then put a cushion under the heel and another at the toes, and bind the patient’s ankles together, and another at the waist, and at the hips, and at the knees; and two assistants should know the ropes, one at the heel and the other at the toes, and they must be well secured, as we have said, and the patient should put his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If it does not return with this treatment, take a spoonful of three hands’ length, and hold the thumb against the side, and let the patient lie on the side; then place the thumb under the scapula and put the middle of the thumb on the spinous process; and place the thumbs of the other hand on the other side of the thumb, and press firmly, until it returns to its place. If you see that it does not, do as the one who turns the hand does.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If you see two tendons at the shoulder of the patient of one hand, and on the pieces two others, and between each tendon there is a knot and a little space of the length of an almond; and in each tendon there is one perforation, or the bone is fractured, and the tendons are firmly fixed in the flesh, so that they do not move; and between two tendons there is one tendon turning, so that the tendon comes out of place; and there are two small tendons of the length of an almond alongside the turning tendon; then the turner must turn the hand until the tendon returns to its place. And the master must put the spinous process even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, if you put on a dry dressing with a lot of eggs, and then press them, and then support it with a tablet of three lengths, that will cause the limb to swell from the hipbone to the spine, and bind it with a thread as we have said, and use the patient some nourishment that is subtle; and if nothing comes to an end of the swelling, if you must administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said above; and never give a dose of lead, and never does it appear at the back of the spine, near the shoulder blade, and take care that this is not a dislocation; and that is the bone that is open, for we must not presume anything: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder never come loose except for simple dislocations, never if there are other joints; and the joint of the hip is damaged in three parts: front and back, and front and back; and the more front it is damaged, the more it is damaged in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is this: when you join the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the patient’s joints than before, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and that is the abscess which is left inflamed with cautery, for that is what causes the head of the humerus to come out of its place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.</start_of_turn
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this is that if the limb is well placed as it should be, although one may see him make a movement of his knee without pain; if this is seen, one must prevent it, and withdraw the urine, and swell the area, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And the sign of that one who has behind him, if he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and his limb is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and he has pain from the hip down to the toes
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three methods of dislocation, if you are hasty and turn the joint, and stretch outwards and downwards, and move forward and backward; by chance it will return, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, know that you must apply one strong minister at the thigh, and at the foot of the limb with two hands, or one that is bound upon the knee; and another minister extends his hand downward as far as it can, while he grasps his hands with his heels; and another holds the head of the limb. Extend both up and down together, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains so.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three out of four cases; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not happen, if you must cure its semblance. When the dislocation is in the armpit, if you can place the patient on his chest, then place the limb on the root of the thigh, and the limb which is beside the groin, then extend the limb upwards towards the armpit, and downwards towards the forcele; then take another minister and grasp his arms, and embrace the great limb of the afflicted thigh, and extend it towards the front: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less harsh than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not tightly bind the limb as we have said, you must know that you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread on the two toes and on the two knees, and that the limb of the patient must be extended two fingers more than the others; then either suspend it on the head of a staff, or on the ground two arms long; then command one minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and another minister to hold the thigh, for the joint is now returning to its natural position.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation has been dislodged, if the patient is conscious, as we have said in the case of hiccuping, grasp the limb firmly above the knee and below the foot; then place two cushions, one at the hip and one at the knee, and insert one cushion between the thighs of the patient in the form of a triangle; then sprinkle damp cloths around, so that the patient does not bleed, and extend the hands of the ministers towards him, and the master places his hand equal to his own on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, it is well.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table and press on it as we have said in the previous discussion, and keep the patient lying on the stone bench.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, if it is necessary to extend the limb greatly, do as I have said; and place your gaze upon the pain, which should be above the painful area, and press with the other hand, and extend from the wrist towards the elbow.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If the dislocation has gone away, if it does not stay in place, do not raise the limb above the ground, but rather that it should be as if it had been loosened previously. As we said before, place the thumb and index finger on the joint; press on the joint with the table; and when the limb extends itself, restore the thighs and place the dressing. Apply a bandage to prevent movement of the limb. Leave for three days or four, then remove the dressing and put on the dressing once more. If you see that the limb is equal, if the bandage is still in place as before, leave for three days; then remove the dressing and leave the limb be until comfort returns to it.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation from the shoulder joint.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is emptied in two ways: that is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards; and do not empty it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if you command the patient to bend his limb to his hip, and he does not stretch it to his hip, the hair that is dislodged will be dry; and when you restore him, if you make the patient sit upright, and extend his limb if he can, and put your hand on his face, and put his heel on your toes; then take his knee to your palms, and draw between your thighs, then bend his two hips together; and another attendant extends his heel, as long as his knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has well bent his limb lightly; and put on the plaster, and make the limb steady at the hip, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, and then take them off. Do not let the patient move until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at a point, if an extension is administered strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the shoulder bone.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The bone is never whole, and never fully dislocated, but is always somewhat bent and fractured.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is dislocated, and try before to the part where it is loosened: bring it back if it is slight, and do it gently with your hands when it is slightly swollen only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dry, if you make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg below the ankle; then bring your thumb to your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, and extend the limb upwards, and keep it well supported; do this twice as we have said, pressing and pulling the limb; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it returns; and if it cannot return, make the patient lie on his back on the earth, and insert your thumbs firmly under his buttocks, and bind his legs together with a sheet, so that he does not move the patient; then hold the patient’s thigh, and another assistant extends the limb with his hands or at the joint, that it lies on the ankle joint; then extend the ankles of both assistants equally, and tie them either at the bottom between the patient’s thighs to retain the patient when it is extended; then put the thumbs equally on the dislocation at the hands, and another assistant holds the leg steady at the ankle, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches a point, if you place the dressing and bind above, and the strain forms, and you tie the limb to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, if the strain; then remove the ligature at the third or fourth day, and tell the patient for three days. If it goes before this end, it is not certain that it will not damage further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he persists in this state, if you must restrain him, as we have said elsewhere, until he is well again.</start_of_turn>
des dois	until he is well again.</start_of_turn>
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if you can manage them well, it is a light matter.</start_of_turn
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the dislocation is not in any knot of the limb, then you must make the patient sit on one leg or on a chair quite straight, and put your limb on what is open of these joints, then press your limb firmly until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is no opening, if you put on the sole of the limb a chair for two fingers, then the strain forms, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Together with wounds and dislocations.</start_of_turn>
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen restored, many times the patient has died: if you are not sufficiently presumptuous in the cure, if you do not know the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and tardy, do not be bold; and at the beginning of things put on a soothing charm, and leave the patient in the hands of the Lord, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you now restore the limb in its place, even as the charm remains; and when the limb is restored, if you administer soothing charms, and cure the wound, as it should be, from dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and the bones are fractured, if the bones are fractured, do as we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering into a state of fear, as I have said, for this is perilous according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your soul and body.
Amen	Amen.
